O sons, when I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by its accomplishment in it and by its expositions and declarations, it has seemed to me that you will understand this treatise, which is a part of the operation with the hand, that is surgery.
For the operation with the hand is spread abroad in our realm and in our time deprived of all, while the science of it perishes, and its vestige is obstructed; and there remain of it only a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have altered the most part and led to errors and confusion, so that the minds of men are closed to it, and its force and art are prolonged.
And it has seemed to me that I should animate this with the arrangement of this treatise in the second place according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that the forms of the instruments of cautery and of other tools of the work might come by addition of declaration, and by preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause why no good artificer is found with his hand in our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and that requires one to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which knows the joints of the members and their forms, and the conjunction and separation of them; and has the knowledge of bones, nerves, and tendons, and the number of these, and the issue of them; and of the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and the places of their issuing.
And therefore Hypocras says that by name is much, but in the work little, and especially in the art of the hand.
But we have already said this in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not learned in what we have said of anatomy, it is not vacated that he may not fall into error by which men will die, as I have seen troops of these, for some are formed in this science and throw themselves from it without experience.
For I saw a foolish and experienced doctor open an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed and the woman died under his hands.
And I saw another doctor who had taken a stone from a man who was in his condition, and the stone was great, and he brought it out with a part of the bladder, so that the man died on the third day.
And I called to take it out, and I saw that by the size of the stone and the disposition of the patient that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who received stipends from a duke of our land for surgery, and he treated a broken black slave; and through the ignorance of the doctor, when he had extracted the fracture, over the wound with poultices and bandages with strong pressure, he did not leave the wound to breathe.
And he did this according to his desires, and he released it, and he bound it for many days and commanded that we should not loosen the bandage; and he did so until the thigh and foot were apostematized, and he came to perdition.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to loosen the bandage, and I obtained tranquillity and he was eased of his pains.
But indeed the corruption was confirmed in the member, so that I could not restrain it, and the corruption did not cease to wander through the member until the man died.
And I saw another doctor who opened an apostema of a canker, and it was ulcerated for some days, until the malice of it was magnified with his lord.
The cause of this is that the black cautery is pure of melancholy humor, therefore it does not come to him with fire from all, but that there be a member which suffers that from all.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation with the hand be considered in two ways: first, in operation which is associated with health; and second, in work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already exhorted this in all parts of this book in which comes operation in which there is error and fear; so that it is necessary for you to guard this and leave that, so that the foolish may not obstruct the way of speaking and disgracing you.
And therefore take up your weapons with solicitude and with protection of God, and your patients with facility and firmness.
And use the better way by the grace of God to health and laudable success, and leave terrible diseases of difficult cure, and bear your arms against that which makes you afraid, so that solicitude in your faith and in your name does not abandon you; for there remain for your glory, and most in the world and beyond to your sanctities.
Gaulish already said in some of his maxims: “Do not heal ill disease, so that evil doctors are not named.”
And I have divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter arranged of the head-to-toe, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter of bleeding and puncturing, and of cupping-glasses, and of bandages, and of extraction of thorns and of their likes, all capitulated and arranged of the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter of restoration and of dislocation, and of cure of torsion and their likes; a chapter arranged of the head-to-toe, and of the forms of the instruments.
I will tell you the quality of the humors of that cautery and the pains of it, and in what complexions cautery is prohibited.
Therefore I say that the term of the quality of the humor of cautery and of the pain of it is long and prolix, and subtle through science, and secret hid; and of it have spoken greatly many sages, and of it are they disagreed, and for me a little suffices of their terms, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cautery confers with all complexions universally the which is of matter or of matter, excepting two complexions, which are cold and moist complexions.
In the cold and dry complexions with matter they disagreed; for some said that cautery is beneficial to it, and others said the contrary of that, that cautery is not convenient in disease which is by quality and by dryness, for nature of fire is quality and dryness, and convenient is that disease cold and dry with that which is cauted and dried be healed.
And I said the contrary of that, that by cautery is made benefit in all disease cold and dry which you see in the bodies of men; for when you compare the body of man and its humidity to the complexions of fire, you rub the body of man moist.
And I speak from experience, as I have tried this myself several times.
However, it is not advisable for someone to attempt this who has not already been instructed and practiced in the art of cautery, and become familiar with the variety of human complexions and dispositions of illnesses within them, and their causes, and the accidents of those illnesses, and the span of time involved.
But in other complexions there is no need for fear, especially in moist and humid illnesses, for all doctors have agreed on these, and they are not at odds over the use of cautery in those.
And know, my children, that the secret of healing with cautery by fire and of its goodness is that cautery is a simple action, the effect of which does not reach except to the member that is cauterized, and it does not affect another member by it except for a little harm.
But the action of a burning medicine reaches to those members from which it is removed, and it strongly brings about an illness in the member that is difficult to heal, and it strongly causes pain.
But fire, by its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that except to make it superfluous. And it is known to us by experience and by long service in the study of art upon the truth of causes; and because of this I am excused from the length of speech. And if it were not for the fact that my free will is not read in this hidden secret of fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies and its expulsion by which illnesses are expelled, in philosophical speech demonstrated, which would be sharpened in your hearts.
And know, my children, that they disagree on the time in which it is convenient to perform cautery and they pause at the best time in spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because the harm from the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of what is drawn by cautery, and especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong and fierce, which do not tolerate delay, so that it is feared that evil may come, which is greater than the little harm that comes from the season.
And yet, do not wonder in your hearts, o my children, at this, for it is not esteemed except by the common people and foolish doctors; it is that to that illness which is healed by cautery, there is not a reduction in time, and they pause at that consequence.
And the cause is not as they think it to be, for cautery is only in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries up the moistness which are causes that bring about pains.
However, cautery surpasses medicine in the strength of its value and the power of its operation and the greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that the illness may return at some time according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness, and the power of it, and what is prepared in the body of it from the aggregation of superfluities in it, and what is come to it in its acquisition in foods and likenesses of those causes; unless that the illness on which cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member with few superfluities and moistness, so that as with cautery for tooth pain and likenesses, it is possible that the pain will not return in him, but what happens in him is small.
And yet, the common speech is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a just speech, not to what they understand about it, for they believe that there is no cure that benefits by medicine nor by any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the intention that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is not except when we administer the manners of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not confer it, and then at the end of the cause we administer man cautery, and it benefits to that. And then from here it happens that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the intention which the commoners and foolish doctors understand.
And they said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not do harm, when it is not absolutely true, for I have already tried this and have proven to you that it does not do this except in some bodies without the others, and cautery with it is good and better than with iron as they said; but when you perform cautery with fire and gold, it is not declared to you, because it is kindled according to the quantity that you desire by the heat of the gold, and because it prepares to receive burn; and if you apply fire on it some leaves so that the craftsman sees by the occupation of that.
And because of this, cautery with iron must be made more gently and closer to the site of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter in cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head into the feet, so that also ask me what you want from him.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers to the moisture and coldness on the servile accident of which there are two causes, it is cause of soda and multitude of flux, called rhachitis, from the head to the tips of the ears and from the ears flowing, and multitude of sleeping, and toothache, and generally of all illness that comes by chill, so as paralysis, palsy, and likenesses in those illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is this: that first you command the patient to be evacuated by laxative medicine the head cleansing, for three or for four days, according to the strength of the patient and his age and habit.
And then command that he shaves his head with a razor, and then let him sit between your hands on a heated bed and let him rest his hands on his feet.
And then place the root of your palm near the foot over the root of the nose between your heels. However, when you have reached the mid-point of that location, mark it with a tent and then apply the olive oil cautery whose recipe is as follows:
And then place this over the marked spot, in such a way that it covers and presses down gently, and you shall keep turning it.
And then lift your hand gently and examine the spot, and if you see some of the bone exposed, with some amount of flesh, then lift your hand again, and if not, return your hand with that iron, with another one of those, if it is cooled off, back to the spot until you see what I have described to you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it over the spot, and let that stay there for three days.
And then place raw meat over it, wrapped in a cloth, and let this stay until the burn scar is destroyed. And then treat the spot with four-ingredient ointment until it is healed.
And they also say that when the plague sores open up, the better the pus flows out, and so it is healthier and more beneficial.
And some of them say that the bone should be cauterized within, and that the cautery should stay until some part of the bone is charred.
And then it should be cut away from the bone, and then treated.
And others say that the cautery should reach down to the nerve, causing strong pressure within the bone until it breaks, and this is the recipe for alphecat in small amounts: And they consider that location to be where the brain's vapors escape from.
And if the plague sore remains open for a long time, then it should be treated until it is healed and consolidated.
But I have not seen these two cauteries used in their entirety except on some men according to the way of fear; and it is better for them as they are, since the head is made transparent by solution of continuity from there, as we have testified in other members, especially when the patient's head is of a phlegmatic nature.
And the first cautery is more gentle and better for them; and it works in this way with advantage.
Chapter according to St.
Of cauterization of the head.
When in every part of the head there is chronic and long-lasting pain, which has been prolonged in the patient, and he uses oils and salves and clysters and poultices and compresses and bandages and other similar remedies without any benefit, then consider that if the patient's head is of a strong constitution by nature, not phlegmatic but having a great deal of heat, then cauterize him with another cautery after the first one. And then cauterize that at the crown of his head with a cautery until the bone is split. The bone split and the amount we have described exposed, then cauterize that with a cautery at the back of the head in the place called the foramen magnum — and it is the location where the ventouse is applied. And move your hand back and forth, and do not expose the bone, for by doing this he will experience great pain unlike with any of the other cauteries on the head.
And I will describe this cautery in its place, for the cautery by which the horns of the head and the occipital are cauterized is more gentle than that cautery by which the middle of the head is cauterized; and this is its recipe:
Chapter three.
Of cauterization for non-ancient hemorrhoids.
When there is pain in the head caused by a cold disorder, or pain within the eye socket, first let it be evacuated with purifying medicines, and let other remedies also be administered as described in earlier diseases; and if nothing helps, then cauterization can be performed in two ways: either cauterization with burning medicine, or with an iron.
But the cautery with burning medicine is that you take a piece of wool and burn it and then put out its ends in both parts of the head. And then prick the location of the pain in the temple with a sharp lance, going deep enough to reach the bone, until it is covered over.
And then press down on it with a tight bandage, and let this remain there for the space of three hours; and then remove the bandage and treat the wound again, letting it heal in two or three days, and then apply raw meat to the spot, covered with a cloth until the wound breaks out.
And then treat that with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines which I have written about in the two sections on burning medicines.
But cauterization by iron is performed like this: heat up the cautery, of which this is the recipe:
And it is called a closed nail, for the head of it is like a small claw with some curvature and in the middle of it is a small prominence.
And then apply it to the place of the pain, and move your hand — so that it is not burned — and turn the iron little by little with speed.
And if the amount that is burned by the nature of the bone is equal to the thickness of it, and you raise your hand so that the artery underneath is not burned, so that there is no flow of blood.
And then dip the cautery in salt water and apply it to the spot for three days; then apply raw meat wrapped in a cloth, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the edge of the blade according to the cautery, and be careful to avoid cutting the artery in this non-ancient hemorrhoid.
Chapter four.
Of cauterization for ancient hemorrhoids.
When you treat hemorrhoids with what we have said about its cure, and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if this cure is unsuccessful, then consider that if it does not yield to this treatment, or to cauterization with medicine, or with fire, then light the cuterry until it turns white, and then press down on it with a bandage, pricking the artery underneath, until it bleeds into the bone.
But you must take care that the jaw is not broken due to chewing, and that no artery is burned and no nerve underneath it, and that no spasm ensues.
And if it is about the caution and protection of blood flow from the artery which is cut, for in the cutting of it there is danger, especially to one who is ignorant, and unaware, let the operation be performed at the beginning.
And I will give you instructions on the course of blood flow from the artery according to its own way, in your own house.
And if you see that this disease does not yield to this cautery and the patient' body tolerates it, then cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have described, and treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you administer the cautery we have described in the section on stretching of the artery with two prongs, then this cautery is better and more effective.
Chapter .V.
Of cauterization for ear pains.
When there is pain in the ear from a cold cause and it is treated with remedies that produce lacrimation and also with other remedies which have been mentioned in the division, and if the pain still persists, then ignite the cautery and it is called punctum, of which this is the form:
And then point to the heat, and move it all around the ear as a wheel is turned, or in circles throughout each part if the pain is in any part. Along with the cautery from the root of the ear, inch by inch as you heat the place with it.
And if the cautery makes ten points all around the ear, and then heals those places in between so that they become healthy again.
Chapter .VI.
Of cauterization for torture.
Torture which is cured by cauterization and not only of the humors that come through phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses.
Avoid cauterization of the humor that comes from dryness or from a spasm in the nerve.
When you cure that kind of torture with syringes and blood-letting and poultices, if your treatment does not work, then apply cauterization to the patient in three places: first at the root of the ear, then a little below his temple, and the third at the junction of two lips.
And apply your cautery opposite to where the pain is, because softening does not come except in the part that appears healed.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize at the right side of the most upper part of the ear, and in the temple another one whose length is according to the length of your finger, and hold your hand with the cautery over it until that quantity of half the thickness of a hair is burnt.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is the specialty of the surgeon, whose form is represented in front of a table. But however more subtle it is that one goes there with the cautery just as it is, and then he puts some on the wound to cover the superficial roughness.
And then cure the place with what is before you until it becomes healthy again.
Chapter .VII.
Of cauterization for old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and you treat it with what we have said but your treatment does not work, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize that person in four places: over both corners of his head, as we have said, and also the middle part of his head, and also cauterize in the throat. And the manner of the cautery is done according to what has been said above.
And you have cauterized on the mouth of the stomach, and it is more difficult to cure; then let it be healed by what comes out.
Chapter .VIII.
Of cauterization for obliteration made by phlegm.
Let the patient receive at the beginning large syringes and purgatives.
And then scrape the whole head of the patient, and place on his throat the ointment described in the treatise on ointments.
And apply that several times because this is the manner of cauterization. And do that according to the methodical order which I have said.
And if he is healed by that then well and good; but if not, then do to him three cauteries in the back part of his head which descend from the highest part of the head to the lowest part of the neck. And apply between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and then cure the cautery with what comes out.
But if you can and the patient can tolerate it, then do to him cauteries in the middle part; and if you see greater tolerance, then cauterize on both corners.
Then cure that until it becomes healthy again; and let the cautery be olive oil according to the form given above.
Chapter .IX.
Of cauterization for parasites and of softening of the whole body.
Let the patient undergo blood-letting of the head with syringes and with what we have said; and then scrape the head of the patient, and cauterize that with cauteries on the middle part of his head, and also cauterize on both corners of his head, and also cauterize on the back part of him, and also do three cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the illness of softening of the body and the patient can tolerate it, then do four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and finally with cautery over what has been burnt, raise your hand. Then cure that until it becomes healthy again, and let this be olive oil.
Chapter .X.
Of cauterization for epilepsy.
Let the epileptic be cauterized only when epilepsy is caused by phlegm.
And let the brain of him be purged at the beginning of his illness with syringes and with other remedies which have been mentioned in the division when the patient is large and can tolerate the exception of the remedies.
And if he is a child who does not take the remedies, then give him poultices and masticables which the servant will apply, before what comes out for several days, with good food.
And then scrape the head of the patient and then cauterize that with one cautery in the middle part of his head according to the previous method, and also cauterize on the occipital bone, and also cauterize on both corners of his head. And if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize him with cauteries which I have said, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and also the vertebrae of the back.
And let this be olive oil according to what precedes it.
But if the patient is a child then apply a subtle cautery according to this method.
Chapter .XI.
Of cauterization for melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupt humidities and gross phlegm, then cauterize that with cauteries which I have said in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excessive decline into melancholy and the body of the patient is humid then let him drink what purges the brain according to what precedes in the division.
And then scrape the head of the patient and also make a decently twisted bandage over his forehead, and then place that over the middle part of his head.
Let the patient be quiet and let him lie on his back.
And then apply a poultice and it is also worthy of being bathed with hot water from sheep. Let that be heated over the fire by moderate heat according to measurement so that it does not suffer when it is put on him. And then apply vinegar in the middle part of his head in the forehead and pour it over so that it runs down.
And do that to him for a week with vinegar, and let him have the other regimen of him until he is healed; or if you wish, cauterize him by making small points according to his strength unless you have your hand with one cautery as it is ordered: this is the cautery which moistens the brain with equality.
And then place that wet cloth in a bowl or in a basin of warm water.
Chapter XII.
Of cauterization with water descending into the ear.
When to you has been revealed the beginning of water in the ear through the signs which I have told in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that cleanses his head, and keep him from all moisture.
And let him sweat in a bath for several days.
And then command him to wash his hair, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle of the head; and then cauterize it with two cauteries over the two temples if the beginning of water is in both ears, or on one side if the water comes from one ear.
Then, with a cautery, cut all the veins and arteries which are below the collarbone; and let the cauteries be in that length in the width of the temples.
And beware of any bleeding when it is cauterized; and if you see any bleeding from it, stop it with some medicine which is possible for you.
And I came with wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries and veins, and cauterization of them and cautioning against bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck below two bones with two cauteries recently produced.
Chapter XIII.
Of cauterization of old tears.
When tears from the ears are old and persistent and through veins and arteries which are in the manifest location of the head and it is verified that this is surplus phlegmatic moisture, then cauterize that with a cautery which we recounted in the chapter on the beginning of water coming into the ears, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries over the temples below two bones. And if you see the need for addition, then cauterize that on all sides of the ear canal at the end of the outer ear with a small cautery.
Chapter XIV.
Of cauterization of blood in the neck for veins and arteries in the neck, and for the throat.
When you treat him with that which we said in the division and your treatment does not profit, then prepare and give the patient a poultice for three nights, and then shave his head, and cauterize it with an olive-oil cautery. And then cauterize that with a cautery of garlic with two cauteries over the two outer ears below the hair, one small.
And beware of the artery that you do not ignite it.
And of the cautery of garlic, this is its form.
Chapter XV.
Of the cautery for softening of the eyelids of the eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by sickness or humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery which has this lunar shape; and this is how you make it:
And if you, cauterize that on the two eyebrows a little bit with two cauteries all divided, and let them be elongated from the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the amount of eyebrow.
And do not press too hard with your hand on the cautery, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid is affected.
Chapter XVI.
Of the cautery for the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are converted into the parts within and close up the eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted into the parts within so that they close up the eye, there are two ways of cauterizing them: one cautery is with fire, and another cautery is with a burning medicine.
If you cauterize it with fire, order the patient to open his eyes so that he cuts his hairs as they grow, while you prolong and burn them; and if he closes it you must strengthen the eye with a bandage so that he does not hurt himself as the hairs are growing.
Then as they grow and burn, put the patient's head in your lap, and then mark on the eyelid of the eyes with a piece of coal, the shape of which is like a leaf of an oak tree, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
And then put cotton soaked in white vinegar or in mullein tea on the eye.
And then light the cautery of which this is the shape.
And then cauterize over the figure which you have marked, little by little, until it burns the surface of the membrane which is like a leaf of myrtle, appearing properly.
And the sign of health from your work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and the hairs of it elevated above the puncturing of the eye.
And then raise your hand and open that for three days, and then put on it a poultice until the scar is healed. And then treat that with ointment until it is healed.
But if they return because of the hairs for some cause, and the eyelid is softened, then do the cautery on it again completely as you did at first.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid, then cauterize that until it is elevated to its natural place and burned and that the hairs do not poke into the eye.
But the cautery with burning medicine is that you order the patient to open his eyes so that he cuts his hairs as they grow and burn; then make the shape of the leaf of myrtle out of cloth.
And then take one ounce of dry salt and a quarter ounce of vitriol. That is: Take this mixture and stir it well so that the vitriol does not stick to the bottom; and then spread this mixture over the cloth which is made in the shape of a leaf of myrtle, and put that on one eye or both; and put under the eye cotton soaked in white vinegar, and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And put the finger over the medicine and press that gently so that he does not hurt himself while the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for it burns in him as fire.
And then when he perceives the burning, let him open it with your finger; and then take away the medicine and wash the eye with water; and then consider if you see the eyelid lifted as it is washed because of the cautery by fire or by cutting, for then it is well; and if not return to that on which the medicine has not bitten and is not blackened until your operation is healed and the eye is contracted.
And then put on it a poultice until the membrane of the cautery is eradicated, and treat that with defynition ointment or other until it is healed.
And it is necessary that you watch over your operation so that no residue of the medicine falls into the eye; and if the eyelid after a few days is softened and for some cause the hairs poke into the eye, then repeat your medicine on that place from which the eyelid is softened, and do it just as you did at the beginning, and bandage him until he is healed.
And this is the shape of a leaf of myrtle:
And know that men's eyes are different in size and smallness, and therefore according to this is your contraction made.
And the way of straightness does not lead to that one who is taught in this art.
Chapter XVII.
Of cautery for the fistula which is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you heal fistula by what we have said in the divisions of sickness and do not trust your healing, then know that you cauterize it according to this way: order the patient to put his head in your lap, and let some servant hold his head between their hands in such a way that he is not hurt nor agitated by his head.
And then put cotton soaked in white vinegar or mullein tea on the eye of him.
And then light the cautery of which this is the shape:
Which is hollow, like the shape of a reed or of a feather of an owl, from one extremity which is made the cautery.
And if you see that it is penetrating to the other extremity. And if you want it to come out like a thread.
However, that which is hollow is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open and draw from him the pus and dry that. And if it is not open, then open it and take out the pus of it.
And then put over it the cautery which is lit, and hold your hand over the eye at the part of the nose so that you or the patient are not hurt, and then put the cautery on the edges of the eye and rub that.
And then if at the beginning of your cautery it penetrates into the bone, well; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice as need is; let him open his eyes for three days, and then put over that a poultice and bandage him until he is healed.
But if after ten days it is not healed, then put over it sharp medicine which erodes the bone and let it be open so that you see the membrane, and scrape it according to what it says in its chapter.
And another way of cautery for the fistula which some first said: stop at the place of the fistula and pierce that and then put in that fissure a thin wire of which the shape is: And melt in that one ounce of lead molten; and hold your hand over the eye with good retention so that he is not hurt as the molten lead does not come to the eye from that; and see that you put on the eye of the patient cotton soaked in white vinegar or water, for the lead erodes the place of the fistula and heal it by a wondrous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about the cautery and the treatment, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to administer an incision in the nose and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose according to where it will go into its proper place.
Here begins the eighteenth chapter.
Of cauterizing the wound in the fistula.
Many times there occur fissures in the lips, and mostly in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you heal those fissures with what we have said in the divisions and your treatment does not work, then light the cautery knife in this way:
And its cavity according to the thinness of the blade.
Then place it gently in those fissures until the cautery reaches the bottom of the fissure.
And then heal that with bandages so that it will be healthy.
Here begins the nineteenth chapter.
Of cauterizing a fistula in the mouth.
When in the root of the uvula or the palate or the roots of the teeth there is an ulcer and it is swollen and broken and old and has a fistula, and you heal it with what we have said about healing but it does not work, then know that you should ignite cautery according to the quantity which was received in the fistula; then put that fire into the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand over it so that the hot iron reaches the bottom of it; and at the end of it make an incision or two; and heal that with what we have said about healing so that it will be healthy.
And therefore if the sore is healed and healthy, that's good; but if not, then it is necessary to discover the place and remove the rotten bone according to what will come in its chapter.
Here begins the twentieth chapter.
Of cauterizing teeth and softening gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are rotten, and you heal them with medicines but they don't work, then put the patient's head in your lap, and ignite the cautery in the form which will come here, in such a way that you place the hook over the tooth and insert into it the ignited cautery quickly, and hold your hand gently over it so that the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And then lift up your hand, and repeat the cautery several times according to what you want.
And then the patient should gargle with salty water and hold it for an hour, and then spit it out; for the rotten tooth is hardened and the softened gum is strengthened, and the corrupt moisture is dried up.
Here begins the twenty-first chapter.
Of cauterizing a toothache.
When a toothache is from coldness, or in it is cold or wormy, or the medicine does not work, then the cautery in that place is according to two ways: either cauterize with cow' hide, or cauterize with fire.
Cautery with cow hide is that you take a cow hide and boil it in an iron pot, and then grab it by the tail and wrap it around the end of the tooth, and then plunge it into the boiling hide and place it quickly on the painful tooth until it is cold.
And then repeat that several times until the goodness of the fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or hide in the said boil, and place it on the painful tooth, and hold the hot iron over it so that the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But the cautery with fire is that you take an iron or ram horn, and it should have some thickness and the heat of the fire not reach the patient' mouth.
And then ignite the cautery in the form which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it so that the cautery is cold; and do this several times because the pain will be reduced or on that day or the next day.
And know that because of that cautery, the patient should fill his mouth with good salive and hold it for an hour, then spit it out; this is the way of cauterizing.
And cauterize with whatever you want according to what is possible for you.
And this is the way of the hook:
Here begins the twenty-second chapter.
Of cauterizing hernia.
When hernias are of phlegm and cold humors and they do not yield to digestion with medicines, and you see that light digestion, then ignite the cautery in such a way that it has two ends bent so that smoke comes out of the cautery through one end, place the ignited cautery on the hernia once, and if it does not yield from that, then hold it over the hernia until the heat reaches the bottom of the hernia.
And if the hernia is small, then place the cautery according to the quantity of the hernia; and then let it cool for three days, and place wool soaked in cow' hide over it so that what the fire has burned is cooled down.
And then heal that with ointment and bandages until it is healthy.
Here begins the twenty-third chapter.
Of cauterizing rawness of throat and constriction of voice.
When moisture comes from the lungs, and especially when it is from coldness of constitution, then know that the patient should be evacuated at the beginning with laxative medicines; then cauterize him from the root of the gullet in the place which has been weakened.
And beware that you do not reach with the cautery to the gullet or burn the membrane of it, but only a little.
And cauterize him with another cautery from the joint of the throat in the last vertebra of it. And the cautery of him should be like a nail, according to the preceding way.
And then heal that with what has been said so that it is healthy.
Here begins the twenty-fourth chapter.
Of cauterizing sickness of the lungs and of coughing.
When coughing and sickness of the lungs are from cold humors, and the patient does not have fever or typhus and it is an old sickness, then cauterize him with two cauteries on the breastbone in the weakened places between the ribs, and with another cautery in the middle place of the chest between the nipples; and let the cautery be like a nail according to the preceding way.
And if you want, let your cautery be punctured by the cautery which is called puncture, the way of which precedes in the puncturing of toothache.
And let the points be inserted into them; and then heal that with what has been said so that it is healthy.
And if the cautery has three bends, for cauterizing is with that: with one cautery you can do three cauteries according to this form:
Here begins the twenty-fifth chapter.
Of cauterizing of thorns which is the head of the helper.
When the helper's head is dislocated from the cause of moistnesses lubricas and it does not return in its hour of its return from the dislocation to him, then know that first reduce the dislocation, and then the patient returns over his shoulder or on his side; and if the joint is dislocated to the parts within with the movements of your left hand, then know that the patient should be raised by the codena which is in the part within with the movements of your left hand, if the joint is dislocated to the parts within.
And then light the cautery having two heads, and this is its shape:
Then cauterize the vein where it penetrates into the other side, and the figure of cauterization comes from four-headed cauteries.
And sometimes it is adjusted according to this count, for which reason they are eight cauteries:
And then put some salt on the cautery and attach the patient to tranquility, and the member must not be disturbed for any length of time until it is comforted:
And if the dislocation is above and below, then it is done like this: cauterize on the muscle with a nail-like cautery or with pointed cauteries, for the joint is confirmed, and moisture is driven out, and the patient is healed.
Chapter .XXVI.
On cauterization of the stomach:
When there comes into the stomach a rubbing and moisture which makes that part to be extruded from its own composition and to be multiplied within it, and if you continue the methods of treatment and do not give relief, then see that the patient lies on his back, extends his arms and legs, and cauterize him with three cauteries: one cautery under the feet for the quantity of a finger with a nail-like cautery, and with two cauteries under the armpits of the cautery, so that the figure of a triangular cautery comes out; and stretch between them so that they are not close to each other to make a wound.
And if the depth of the cautery is the quantity of two fingers or as thick as the vein:
And the figure of the cautery is according to this shape with its addition, and if you want, cauterize in the middle of the stomach with a large cautery in this shape; and that one be a cautery according to the shape of a circle like this:
And the stomach is punctured at the place where it is frightened by that cautery: and you feel on the stomach a point according to the quantity you want with a thread, and then cauterize it with a cautery on the points; and then treat it with the treatment which has been preceded so that it is healed.
Chapter .XXVII.
On cauterization of a fretted liver:
When there is pain in the liver from rubbing or moisture or grossness and it is extruded from its normal composition by superfluous egress, and the patient is treated as we have said and does not confer with that, then see that the patient lies on his back on his head, and feel with a thread three cauteries according to this shape and quantity placed on the liver below the hypochondrium on the right side:
And let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be according to the length of the body straight.
And do not move it with the cautery.
And if the quantity of that which is burned is the quantity of half a thread of the thickness of the vein, and it is not close together; and if the patient stands on his feet, and if he does not stand, then let him lie, having already extended his limbs and elevated his arms:
And you have the ability to cauterize these cauteries with a cutlass cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art:
And beware that you do not go too far in cauterization and that the thickness of all the vein is burned so that it reaches into the intestines, for the vein is here subtle; know this.
Chapter .XXVIII.
On boring of an abscess of the liver with a cautery:
When there is an ulcer or abscess on the liver and you want to know whether that abscess is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic, then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the patient will groan heavily and pain will be sharpened:
And if it is in the tunic of the liver, with great pain increased several times so that the doctors tire from curing him:
Then see that the patient lies on his back on his head; and then feel the place of the abscess with a thread; and then light the cautery which is assembled like a rag, the shape of which has been preceded in the other page: And cauterize with that cautery until all the vein is burned so that it reaches into the spleen, where bile flows:
Then treat him with treatment for the other abscesses until he is healed.
And do not use this form of cautery except that one by which the study in the art of medicine is prolonged, and many diseases are known from it; but rather let us know that one, for although sometimes it is tried on this operation, it is better.
Chapter .XXIX.
On cauterization of a hernia:
Dissent the ancient cauteries of the roots of aristology for hernias with a rub according to this manner, and it is this which you take from the roots of aristology: a long, dry root that is found, and it is as thick as a finger:
And then immerse it in oil and heat it in the fire, and then cauterize with a cautery on that place which is between the continuance of the furcula and the collar-bone; and with two small cauteries below the guids, one slightly declining to the part where the beard is, and with two cauteries on what declines between the fifth rib and the breast-bone, declining a little to behind; and with a cautery in the middle of the foot; and with another over the stomach; and with three cauteries on the parts behind; and with a cautery in that place which is between the two shoulders, and with two cauteries on the sides of the leg, below the cautery which is between the two shoulders.
And do not move your hand with the cautery but let it be in the evident appearance of the vein as it appears:
And they have also said some ancient things which are of men whose cauteries of iron are like a ray and heated that, and put it in that place which is between the ribs so that it reaches to that abscess, and it is foreseen bile, as we have said in the abscess of the liver:
But in this boring with a cautery there is no fear, for it happens to them at once in the place where a fistula appears to which there is no cure:
Chapter .XXX.
On cauterization of a hernia:
When you cure the illness of a hernia with what we have said about the division and do not confer your cure, then cauterize him according to three ways which are all right, one of which is that you make three cauteries or four lines according to the length of the hernia according to the figure of the cauteries of the liver, the figure of which has preceded:
And let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger or a little more, and the manner of the cauterization is the same as we have said in the cauterization of the liver with a straight edge:
And do not move your hand with the cautery, and let the patient lie on his back.
And another manner of cauterizing is that you ignite the cautery having two verminents, which cause has been said in the chapter of dislocation of the muscle, and elevate the vein which is in the end of the hernia where the patient’s left hand is:
And let your elevation be such that you raise the patient according to the length of their body, so that cauteries can be applied according to the breadth of the body.
Then insert the two hot rods into the space through which you have penetrated the patient from the other side.
Then withdraw the cautery; and thus are made four cauteries.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three rods.
And then you treat the cautery until it has ceased to smoke for several days, because it is more beneficial than the other previous causes in the cure.
Chapter 31.
Of cauterization for dropsy.
Cauteries should not be used for dropsy except in the intestines specifically.
When you treat the dropsical person by the methods of cure which we have stated in the division, and do not make your cure concordant, then you should cauterize four cauteries in the circuit of the groin, and a cautery over the stomach, and another cautery over the liver, and another cautery over the spleen, and two cauteries between the vertebrae of the back, and a cautery in the right side of the abdomen, and another cautery over the stomach. And the quantity of the depth of the cautery should be proportionate to the thickness of the body.
And then withdraw the cautery so that it smokes for a long time.
And do not discharge the patient of the cure by the cautery with that which has been used so that two tendencies are added to him and he is helped to health by them.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be key-shaped according to that which is above it previously, and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped according to that which precedes it.
Chapter 32.
Of cauterization for feet and the thighs.
When the feet are swollen with dropsy and filled with yellow water, you should cauterize the feet over the instep of the foot in between the ring finger and little finger, and elevate your hand with the cautery and do not twist it; then elevate your hand and do not return it at all, for the yellow water flows.
It is cauterized in this shape: and then make two cauteries over both thighs, and in each thigh there should be made a cautery with the end of the cutlass-like cautery. And let the cautery be according to the length of the thigh: one above the knee and the other below, and on each thigh two cauteries.
Then withdraw the plague after the cure for a long time so that no water flows from him.
And then treat it with those causes which we have stated.
Chapter 33.
Of cauterization for body of the belly.
When the body of the belly is affected by rubbing and moisture which weakens the intestines, there is digestive and retentive vertigo, which are in the stomach and intestines, and it is cured with the methods of cure and not concordant, and sometimes the patient suffers from vertigo of excessive heat, then cauterize him with a large cautery over his stomach according to that which precedes in the cauterization of the stomach, with the cautery of the circle and four cauteries in the circuit of the groin with subtle key-shaped cautery; and cautery over the anus over an ulceration great, or with two cauteries.
And if you see the excessive moisture and the patient can tolerate it, then cauterize him over the penis and over the intestines, and tightly press two cauteries over the stomach and near the groin, for that is a perfect cure of generation from which one does not err.
Chapter 34.
Of cauterization for old hemorrhoids.
When in nature there remain old hemorrhoids or one of gross humors rubbing or of corrupted moisture, and they are cured with that which we have stated in the division and do not concordant with your cure, then cauterize with three cauteries over the pus below the small vertebra of the back triangularly, and cautery above the navel through two holes.
And if it seems that his stomach is rubbed and his food is not digested, and his face is sometimes swollen, then cauterize him over the stomach with a large cautery according to what precedes; and a cautery over the liver, and another cautery over his spleen with key-shaped cautery, and withdraw the cautery for some time, then cure him so that he is healed.
Chapter 35.
Of cauterization of atheyl near its incision.
When you excise atheyl, then you heat the cautery which is assembled with wax. Then place it burning into that atheyl which is excised, and finish your hand until it reaches the opening of the vein from which comes the blood.
And do this once or twice, for if they are several, then cauterize each of them according to what we have recounted, and then cure those with that which agrees with them in the wounds until he is healed.
And if you cauterize with a large cautery over an ulceration, it is better for generation.
Chapter 36.
Of cauterization of fistulas which are made in nature through openings in him.
When nature does not obey the work which we have commanded in its place, and the patient is frightened by that, then let him be healed by cautery.
Therefore when one sees a fistula in nature through, and it is old, draw the pus from him and corrupted moisture, and therefore what is best to do is to probe him with a subtle probe, then know the quantity of its depth by that which has been stated before.
Then heat the cautery which is like wax. Then place that cautery burning in this fistula according to the quantity in which it entered the probe.
And repeat the cautery over that until those putrefied bodies are burnt one time or two or three according to your need.
And beware of burning nerve and vein; or if the fistula goes to the bladder or to the intestines, then beware of all those places; and do not do that unless the fistula is in fleshy place and you are sure that it does not penetrate.
And then cure that place until it is healed.
And if the place is sealed and the matter has been excised from him and it has healed for a long time, then know that it is entirely cured.
And if the matter is not excised from him, then know that it is penetrating or in his preons are corrupted, or sends something of those causes which will bring a reminiscence to its place.
Chapter 37.
Of cauterization for warts.
When in warts there is pain from rubbing or from grossness and moisture, and the flesh of the patient is damaged, then cauterize those over the warts with a cautery over each wart with key-shaped cautery from which you predict the reminiscence.
And then tightly cauterize with the second a little below, so that three cauteries are linear, and therefore they will be better for generation.
Chapter 38.
Of cauterization of the bladder.
When it happens to the bladder weakness and softness due to friction and moisture so that the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize that area below the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, and cauterize with one cautery on the right side, and another on the left.
And the length of each cautery should be according to the size of the testicles; and cauterize that area with one cautery below the buttocks, or with two cauteries if necessary.
And let the cauteries be like nails according to how they are applied.
Chapter 39.
Of cauterization of the thigh.
When there is moisture and softness in the thighs, and due to this pregnancy is prohibited, and their menstruation is corrupted, and their induction is delayed, and pain occurs from carrying them, then let the area be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, just as we have said in the cautery of the bladder; and with one cautery above the buttocks, or with two cauteries, and let the cautery be like a nail.
Chapter 40.
Of cauterization of the dislocation of the hip.
When moist humors are infused into the hip joint, and this is caused by the displacement of its place, and a sign of it is that the thigh is prolonged over the other when compared between them. And the location of the dislocation is obstructed in the spot where it hurts.
Therefore let the patient be cauterized over the hip joint with a round cautery like a ring, after you have marked it with a tent in the circuit of the joint as it is turned, and because of this the joint falls into the middle of the circle.
And let the cautery be of that shape of which we spoke in the cauterization of the stomach.
And if this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize that area with three cauteries using a large olive-shaped cautery.
And let the cautery be made according to the quantity of the thickness of all the tendons; and then heal that area after it is cured.
Chapter 41.
Of cauterization of the sciatic nerve.
When pain comes in the hip joint, and its cause is friction and moisture, it is cured with what we have said and does not return, and that is old, then let the patient be bled of gross humors with fetid pills or artificial pills or similar; and then cauterize that area.
And the manner of the cautery in that is according to two manners: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
They go according to two known manners, of which one is that you cauterize that area over the hip joint with three triangular cauteries according to this shape; and make them good and deep. And let the space between each cautery be the quantity of the thickness of the finger, and if the cautery is olive-shaped or large.
But sometimes let the cautery be over the middle joint of the hip so that there are four cauteries.
And if you want, cauterize with the ring of which we spoke in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, and that is a containing circle and burns the thickness of all the tendons.
And this is the manner of cautery in sciatica when pain is attached to the hip and is not extended within the thigh.
But if it is extended within the thigh, then cauterize that area with two cauteries over the thigh over the spot where the pain lies; and with one cautery over the ankle four fingers from the wild side.
And if the cautery is cut, then let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of the thickness of the tendon.
And if the pain goes from that area where it lies within the foot by three or four or more points, then cauterize that spot with a cautery in three places or four or more if it is needed.
And if the pain goes from that area below the knee to the thigh, then cauterize that spot with one cautery cut.
And beware in every cauterization that you do not burn with the cautery any nerve or large artery, and because of this there is harm to you or contraption upon it.
And you have seen one and another of those who cauterized over the ankle and ended in cauterization, and the fire was inflamed within which the tumor was achieved by the foot, and the fire pierced and corrupted all the foot. And then a strong solution of the belly occurred, and then death followed.
And if the pain is in two places at once, then cauterize each according to this manner.
And the wise say in cauterization of the hip that this is the manner of the cautery: make like a ring of iron of which the circuit is the size of a palm; and let its orifices be according to the thickness of a fingernail or more than a little.
And within that circle let there be another third; and let the space between them be the size of the testicles; and those circles are exposed in two places; and let the length of those nails be one or two fingers, and make on those edges of iron decently wrapped in the circles; and this is the shape of it:
Then let it be ignited in fire within that it is curved and emits sparks, and then let it be laid upon the spot of the hip, the pain lying upon its side. And thus cauterize that area with three round cauteries in one go.
And then let it lie for three days; and then plaster that area with wool and let the wound remain open for several days; and then heal that area after it is cured.
Albucasis says: O sons, of this kind of cautery we have used few for the sake of his guard, and because of it we have found few who guard him.
But of the many cauteries which afflict him, and that spot upon him.
But cautery with burning medicines is that you make two circles having a perforated armlet in which the hook of the door of iron is placed; let the length of their edges be two nuts or nails.
And if the space between each of them is the quantity of the thickness of the finger; and let them be exposed below and above, and let them contain themselves according to this shape:
And then let it lie over the hip joint the pain lying upon its side, and press your hand upon the spot of the hip; and then take cold water and pour it between two circles, and let its quality be by the fire little by little, and let that afflict him the biting and the squeezing of it — for that which inflicts biting as well as fire — until the biting stops.
And then raise your hand by the instrument and wipe off cold water from all over the hip with warm water.
And then let it lie for three days and let him rest upon that bandage until the blackness of the squeezing is gone, and let him lie for several days, and let the swelling of him depart; this is the last in healing.
And then heal that area after it is cured.
And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, have him lie on his side containing water as is done in the armpit similarly.
And this is the manner of water bath, and I have already written about it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take an equal amount of alkali and caustic not extinguished from both, crush them and place them in a new pot of which the bottom is perforated with a small hole according to the quantity that goes into it.
And place below the bottom of the pot another pot covered, and pour over the alkali and live caustic sweet water which collects it through a finger, and since you compress it with your hand by good compression, and let the hot water flow from it into the pot below.
And then collect all that water, and pour it over another live caustic and renewed alkali, because that time it will be of a very strong acidity, which is administered in many operations of medicine and in cauterization of the other members, because this operation is done by fire.
And some medicines with which it is cauterized widely, such as tetter and honey of vinegar mixed with soap, so that they are mixed.
And Gualia recorded from a man of the ancient operation and the cure by which it is healed pain in the armpit and sciatic vein, and magnifies very much that one, and says that no other cure is needed, and because it is healed with one wash and hot bath as well, for he has known that one.
And it is to be taken from a certain ragwort, and if not found, then take fig recently; and it must be crushed with a little grease and placed on the armpit where there is pain, or in the thigh, or leg, and be bound.
And it is to be left for the amount of three hours or for the quantity that the patient can bear the tightness.
And then put him in a bath and when his body is relaxed, place him in the sun, because the pain will cease and he will be healed.
And know that there is no doubt that anyone uses cautery with these medicines except for the evacuation of the body.
But Escorides said that when with goat's gall the sciatic vein is cauterized, it would be beneficial to him; and the cautery on him should be according to this way: wool should be taken and dipped in old oil, and placed between the big toe and the second toe.
And then take dry goat' gall and inflame it with fire into a charcoal; and then place it on the wool and let the fire go out. And then repeat this, and do not cease doing this until the sensation of the bite comes into the armpit and stops the pain.
And this way of cautery is called cow's cautery.
Chapter .XLI.
Of cauterization for pain in the throat.
Sometimes pain is in the back for various reasons, such as from a blow or piercing or from excessive discharge, and because of causes like these, from infusion of moist matter.
And cauterize not at all except in this sole species which is made by effusion of moist matter.
Then, appropriate evacuation of the patient with blisters and like them, which are made on the back in which there is pain in three lines according to its width, since you mark with a tent in each line for cauterization or not, according to the quantity that comes from the tolerance of the patient and of his strength.
And cauterization is to be done by pointed cautery.
And if you want, cauterize with three cauteries or four with mid-sized cautery according to this form:
Chapter .XLI.
Of cauterization for the beginning of goiter.
Many times this malady happens to small children, and sign of the beginning in children is that there occurs to them constriction in the neck by elevation and movement.
And press on the last vertebra of the back and on the notches of it that already begins to rise above the others vertebrae.
And therefore when you see this and want to prohibit, then cauterize that with circular cautery according to this form: that the cautery takes on both sides of the vertebra evenly.
And if you want, cauterize in the circuit of the vertebra with pointed cautery two lines or three. And the points are close to each other.
And then cure the place within which has been healed by what we have said.
But be careful that cautery is not administered in goiter that is made by spasm of nerve.
Chapter .XLI.
Of cauterization for gout and for pain in the joints.
When pain in the joints is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
And therefore when gout caused by moist matter is healed by the way of cure and not gone away the pains, then they are cauterized.
And it is that you cauterize that after evacuation in the circuit of the joint of the foot with many cauteries.
And cautery oil of which this is its form:
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pains penetrate into the joints or the other joints, and this happens many times, then cauterize that on each toe with three cauteries or four from all sides with this cautery oil.
And if many cauteries that these cauteries are necessary to you, then cauterize that and do not press too much your hand on the cautery before, but only wrap around the end of the cautery.
And if the pains penetrate into the toe and the back, then administer the cautery which we have said in its chapter.
And if the pains are only in the hands and it is called arthritis, then puncture on the surface of the knuckles as they rotate, puncture them two lines.
And if remain of the pains in the fingers, then puncture on the circuit of the knuckles on each joint and on the palm.
And if the pains penetrate into the bones or the muscles, then cauterize all parts of the joints.
And do not evacuate the patient from good regimen and reception of medicines, because if good regimen and phlegm is evacuated by this cautery it will be healed, God helps.
Chapter .XLI.
Of cauterization for broken bones.
When there is broken bone in the angles and they say the intestines within the chest of the child, and this is the beginning from within, then know that you order the patient to stop his food for the day and use healing causes for it so that the crack goes away from his belly.
And then follow the patient between your hands on his back, and command him that he has his mouth within that it is split or appears the skin or the bones.
And then return that by his fingers and know that you point out the fracture on the bone of the finger by pointing to the extremity which is similar to the tip of a circle in the upper parts of the body.
And then light the cautery of which this is its form:
while it is still wet, let it drip into the wound and repeat several times. Then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area to prevent the intestine from coming out.
You have already opened the space between the patient's thighs, placed a cushion under them, another servant on their legs, and another on their chest, holding their hands.
And then place the cautery over that mark with your hand holding the cautery straight, and push into the wound until you feel the bone of the testicle within the scrotum; and repeat with the other testicle if you have not managed it on the first try.
And be very careful with the movement of the intestine during the cauterization, lest you burn it and cause death or some other great harm to the patient.
And know that when you are using the cautery, if you do not feel the bone, your operation is pointless.
And know that the cautery for children should be fine according to their size.
Then treat the site of the cauterization for three days by applying a plaster once the burn scar has healed.
Then treat it with other ointments until it is healed.

And then place the two ends of the bile, one end that goes over the nose and the other that goes into the nose, and then administer the cutting of meat with the nuts that are in the bile, and do this until you know that the meats have been cut by the nuts of the bile.
And then pull out the bile and place in the nose the abstraction of the blood a cauterization, and do this for three days or more until the paint corrodes everything that is left of the meat.
And then at the end of the cure, place in the nose a lead tube for several days until it has healed.
But if you find that the cure is dried out, use that one.
And this is the form of the instrument of a purging cupping-glass with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils.
And do this from silver or copper, which is like a small open lamp, just like a small hole, and the meat similarly.
And if you want, make a closed tube just like a cane, and the cup of the purging cupping-glass be flat and uncovered; to which is handled at its end, with which you have that when you heat it in it oil or water that you want from the juices and the sucking causes.
Chapter 25.
Of ulcers in the ends of the nose.
Many times an ulcer is born in the ends of the nose, and it is magnified and swollen for several days until it comes to a head.
And for this cause you pierce that in the beginning of its appearance, and drain all of that. And then place on the spot a cauterization or burning medicine which is placed in the location of it.
But if its piercing is delayed until it has become magnified, then consider that it has suppurated, has become hard, of a dark color and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron which is the cranky ulcer; because many times when you pierce this ulcer in that way great malice comes upon him who.
And if the ulcer is of lion touch and not of dark color, and its piercing is possible in all of that, then discharge the patient and pierce it with fearlessness, and heal the spot with what drips out and constrict it until it has healed.
Chapter 26.
Of the sewing of the nose and of the lips and of the auricle when the continuity is dissolved by a ulcer or similar.
Know that when solution happens in one of these cartilage, few confer in that operation except in some men.
Therefore, when for any cause of those, you consider that it is fresh blood with your blood, then sew the two lips of the ulcer with sewing, and then heal it until it has healed.
And if the lips of solution of continuity are already separated, and each is healed, then cause that you cut each part of its apparent tendon until blood comes out. And then sew the two lips with sewing and strengthen those, and on top of them pulverize blood of dragon and unmixed ashes, and place on the powder a piece of emplaster diafinicon, or of any other of the consolidating plasters, and let that lie for two days or three, and then remove that and change that plaster and let it lie until the sores are healed.
But the manner of sewing is that you add the solution of continuity or with needles just as we have mentioned in the sewing of the belly, or add the solution of continuity with bile just as I have told.
Chapter 27.
Of the extraction of those causes that come in the two lips in the parts inside.
Many times in some men in the parts inside of their lips there are some hard ulcers like grass of worms, and some are small and some are large.
Therefore cause that you turn the lips and split each of those duress from all parts, and then the piercing fill up the place with ground sage within that the blood is restricted, and then wash it with vinegar and let it be healed by what has been constricted, until it has healed.
Chapter 28.
On the beginning of meat being chewed on the gums.
There are blisters on the gums which the ancient ones called albus, then you should suspend that with tweezers or what you have, and pinch its root, and let the pus flow out or the blood.
Then place on the spot sage that has been cut up into pieces or another powdery astringent or caustic.
And if the meat comes back, then you should cut it again secondarily and cauterize it, for then the cautery will not come back.
Chapter 29.
On the reason for teeth with iron.
When in the surface of the teeth of the molars and of the incisors, and between the gums are found rough scabs, callouses, and some blisters that are blackened and are made citrine or green within which causes corruption to the gum, and these callouses are made thus.
And so you should make the patient open his mouth between your hands and place his head in your lap, and rub the teeth in which these scabs appear, and cause them to become like sand, so that no other cause remains within them, and this is what makes the blackness and citrinity and others within so they are cleansed.
So if this is left as in the beginning of the process, it is good; and if not then you should repeat the process over them another day, or on the second or third within which it comes to its final state in what you will.
And know that teeth have need of many резоры of diverse forms and of many figures according to how they are prepared for your operation. And thus the rasp used for the tooth to be rasped on its molars side is another than that used for rasping between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of rasps you should prepare them immediately as you will see.
Chapter 30.
On the removal of teeth.
You should cure the tooth of its pain with every remedy and delay in its total removal as there is not any cause that prevents the growth of it when removed, for this is a sublime substance that is excused in its removal.
But when the patient is forced to have that tooth removed you should be certain which is the painful tooth, for many times pain deceives the patient and it seems as if it is in a healthy tooth, and you remove that one and the pain does not cease until the diseased and painful tooth is removed, for we have already seen this through operation of the gums.
So when you are certain which is the painful tooth and that you know well, then you should scrape around the circuit of the tooth with a spathe in which there is some virtue so it is dissolved from the gum all around, and then cut that with your fingers or with thin forceps little by little until you concavitate it.
And then grab it firmly with strong tweezers for good speech or stupor strongly, and place the head of the patient between your thumbs which you hold well so he does not move, and then pull the tooth according to rectitude in a manner that you do not break it, nor give greater pain to the patient.
And so if it is not loose, then take one of those instruments and place it beneath all around with ease and force the removal of it thus as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is split or rotten then you should cover that split with a cloth and press it with the end of a thin ray so that it is not broken in the hour of your constriction on it as you hold it with tweezers.
And you should open completely by scraping all around the gum and guard much of your strength that you do not break it or cause a split to form from it, and return upon the patient for the wickedness he has done to him.
And guard yourself that you do not do as unskilful barbers do in their foolishness and audacity on the removal of them, who do not administer what we have recommended; for many times they bring upon men great diseases which are more difficult than to be broken, or that you extract those with some bones of the jaw thus as we have testified.
And then the removal of it is washed in the mouth with wine or vinegar and salt.
And if it still flows blood from there then take some quantity of chalk and sprinkle on the wound, and if that chalk does not help then cauterize.
The form of the forceps and tweezers which are used to pull out the tooth at the beginning is of long length, short handle and thick, so that they are not bent when you operate with them.
And let it be thus as the gross handle within that when you stretch with them they are not bent and are short lengths.
And let it be made of iron from India descendingly made from right angles and in the angles of those there are teeth of which some enter into each other and stretch by strong constriction, and sometimes the angles of those are in the form of a goose beak which has the name ciconia, it is hooked, and they are of strong constriction.
