Chapter 32.
Of the cure of teeth that protrude above the others.
When teeth are prominent, not according to their natural form, and especially when this occurs in women, and most especially in elderly women; therefore you should consider: if a tooth is adjacent to another tooth, and it is not possible to cut or file it down, then extract that tooth. But if it is attached to another tooth, then you insert into that tooth an instrument of which this is the shape, and it is similar to a pig's jaw, and it should be made of very acute Indian iron.
And you should make your incision in such a way that you insert it into the tooth for several days according to the hardness of the tooth, and so that no other tooth is affected.
And if there is an prominent tooth exposed to filing, then file it with Indian iron file of which this is the shape:
And it should all be made of Indian iron, both the edge and the handle; and it should have very fine points like a file with which needles are made, with which the tooth is filed little by little over several days with ease, so that no other tooth is affected and falls out. Then smooth it at the end, and shave it with a very sharp razor.
And if there is a tooth of which one part is broken and cuts the tongue, then you should smooth that so that the sharpness of that fracture is removed and blunted, and it is flattened so that the tongue is not cut nor speech impaired.
Chapter 33.
Of the restoration of broken teeth with gold or silver foil.
When there is a concussion and displacement of the teeth due to a blow or falling, and the patient cannot bear to bite down on it, and your treatment with astringent medicines has not worked, then so that they do not fall out, it is useful to strengthen them with gold foil rather than silver, for silver turns black and rots after a few days, but gold never changes.
And the foil should be of such thinness and thickness according to the quantity that can fit between the teeth; and the technique of this is that you take the foil and place twice as much between two healthy teeth, and then let it grow with two twists of the foil between two broken teeth, or if one or several, until the material reaches the healthy tooth on the other side. Then repeat the twisting between the part from which you began, and strengthen your hand with ease and skill so that it is not broken.
And your twist with which you strengthen the foil should be between the roots of the teeth so that it does not escape.
Then cut off the excess foil with tweezers or tongs, and join those ends together with wax, and conceal them between the healthy tooth and the broken tooth, so that they do not hurt the tongue. Then let it set tightly like Roman cement.
But if it is loose or broken, strengthen it or those with other foil in the same way at all times.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the twist between two healthy and two broken teeth, as follows:
And when one or two teeth are pushed back into their sockets due to a blow, and they have grown back as we have described, and they break again:

Chapter 34.
Of the incision of the membrane which comes in the tongue and prohibits speech.
This membrane which comes underneath the tongue sometimes occurs naturally or accidentally and happens due to a wound that has already healed.
And the operation on it is that the patient opens his mouth, and you raise his tongue, and then cut that nervous membrane according to the width so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment.
But if there is any hardness or knotting, and it has been caused by the hardening of a wound, then you heat oil and cut that according to the width through which you cut the membrane so that the knot is dissolved.
And be careful that there is not a tear in the flesh of the lip and that you split the membrane and cause blood to flow.
Then wash the area of the incision with wine or vinegar or water rubbed with vinegar, and then place the tongue in a relaxed position; this is what the patient should do every night so that it does not harden again.
But if blood flows from it, place powdered vitriol on the spot; but if the blood clings to it, then cauterize the area with a red-hot cautery that is appropriate for this. Then treat it with the other causes so that it heals.
Chapter 35.
Of the extraction of a ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes there occurs underneath the tongue an apostema similar to a small onion that prohibits the tongue from its natural movement, and it is enlarged when it fills the mouth.
And the operation on it is that the patient opens his mouth widely and you examine the apostema.
And if you see it of a dusky or black color, hard, and the patient feels nothing, then do not touch it because it is rotten.
And if it is inclined toward whiteness and there is moisture in it, then you put oil on it, and cut it with very thin spatulas, and cut it all around; and if blood flows when you operate on it, then you place powdered vitriol on it, so that the blood is constricted.
Then return to your work so that it has been treated with wine and salt, and treat it with the other treatment so that it heals.
Chapter 36.

And if it is red-colored and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron because of the flowing blood; before you let it set so that it hardens, then either you will pull it out or break it up itself.
And if it is white-colored and the root is thin, then that is what should be cut.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, if the apostema has rested due to being cauterized with complete rest or if it has diminished due to any diminution; and then let the patient open his mouth in front of the sun, and his head be in the usual position, and the servant place his hands between their knees, and the server press the tongue of the patient away from below with a noble instrument of which this is the shape:
Let it be made of silver or of bronze, and let it be thin as a needle.

Another thing is that you should withdraw some cause from the membranes, and then cut into that with an instrument in the form of which this is. and is like a pair of tongs, except that the ends of it are bent, so that the aperture of each one is facing that of the other, very sharp, and made from iron which has been tempered.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then cut into it with a spatula, of which the shape of this is: and let it be sharp on one side, but not on the other.
And then after you have cut one slit, cut the other according to this manner of cutting, and then let the patient be healed from water which has been rubbed.
But if there is bleeding instead, then heal it with water of the cooking of the husk of a pomegranate or of the leaf of a myrtle and similar to that of the causes which constrict within so that the flow of blood is restricted, and then cure that until it is healed.
And sometimes it is seen in the gullet other ulcers other than those two ears, and cut into those according to what I have said about the cutting of two slits evenly.
And I have already treated a woman of an ulcer which had come in her throat, that ulcer extending to the color brown, with little feeling, and which had already closed her throat, and the woman was breathing with difficulty, and had already prohibited eating and drinking water, and she had already been brought to death if not for one day or two.
And the ulcer had pushed so much that it had caused two bumps where pus came out through two holes.
Therefore I cut into it skillfully and put my finger in one of them, and I drew out that, and a great portion came out of him, and then I cut into that where I understood the other hole to be, and then I bound his mouth, and pressed his tongue, and then I put my finger in that ulcer.
And then I cut away a great portion of it, and not much blood ran from him but a little. And then the throat of that woman was freed, and she began immediately to drink water, and then took food, therefore I did not cease cutting into that ulcer many times over a long time, and another ulcer came in place of that one which I cut while it was prolonged.
Therefore I cut and cauterized her throat again, therefore after a few days; and then I wandered and did not know what God had done to that, therefore I am astonished.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of cutting of the veil when it is ulcerated.
When there is discharge from the membrane and it is ulcerated and long, then it is called a perpendicular ulcer; and if it is in the part below thick and round, then it is called a bubo.

But if that instrument is not available to you, then take a cane and put at the end of it a plug of wood, so that the mouth of the patient be bent, for the plug of wood prohibits the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is beneficial for health.

Chapter 40.
Here is the translation of the text:
Abscesses are many kinds, from many sources, as one will see in this book.
And they differ in their opening and section by two ways, one of which is through the nature of the abscess itself; the other is through the moisture that is contained within it.
And the second way is according to the location in which they occur, for an abscess on the head is different from one that occurs on the bottom; and an abscess at a muscular site is different from one that occurs at a joint; and each of these has its own treatment through operation.
And among abscesses there are some which should not be opened, but rather allowed to mature until the pus is discharged from them or they are completed.
And there are other abscesses which should be opened when they are cross; and they are not matured according to their nature, such as abscesses that are near joints, for an abscess when it approaches a joint, its essence is prolonged into the pores of its surroundings, and strongly corrupts the tendons or nerves of that joint, through which there occurs contraction of that member; or it is an abscess near a principal member, and if you delay its opening until it matures, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the bottom, therefore open it so that it does not mature, but rather one that is near the bottom, so that its pressure may not increase, lengthen into the parts within the bottom, and a fistula be made, or that there be made in the end of it what may not heal. But you should know the time of opening an abscess, and that is when it has matured.
And you should know that it is matured when there is a decrease in pain and fever, and an approprate decrease in heat and pulse, and the sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And because you should know the opening to be made in the most low part of the abscess and from pus coming from the healing of the eminence.
And the opening is always to be made through the length of the flesh or the body, if the abscesses are in parts of the hands or feet, and at places of the veins, of the cords of the nerves, of the tendons; and, finally, in all places alike from which there is reflection; for those in which there is reflection, use opening according to that member.
But when the abscess is at a muscular site, it is better that you delay its opening until its digestion is confirmed according to its nature; for if you open it before this, there will be lengthening of the pore of it and much filthiness, and strongly the lips of it will be hardened and its depth.
But some abscesses are opened according to the breadth of the flesh or the body through necessity, or according to that of which the member is in need.
And you should administer small opening in small abscesses, and large opening and ample or many incisions in great abscesses according to the diversity of their size.
And others are of abscesses in which the membrane is hollowed out and incised when it has been made in such a way that bread is done to it, and it is done in term that it was already, as well as that which occurs in trops of doubt and of blisters.
And of those there are that are cut with three angles; and of those in which it is cut in the figure of a bay-leaf, as well as the abscesses of the angles.
And there are some in which round section and lunar section is administered, and similar to those.
But that at which there is not head as of superficial abscesses, you should open it with superficial opening or plain incisions only.
And when the abscess is great and has collected much pus, you should open it and not be afraid to extract all of its pore in that hour; after having extracted some from it, you should then pack the abscess so that there is a filling within it for another day, and again after having extracted a greater part, you should do this many times according to degree until it is foro-getat.
And especially if the patient is of weak nature or a pregnant woman, or small child, or old in decrepitude, for the animal spirit is many times resolved by the exit of pus, and strongly the patient dies, and you operate on them.
Therefore guard this chapter with great caution, and when you open the abscesses in which you operate on these abscesses, after having washed the wound consider if there is little pus or the section is flat, then administer leeches of larch or oak-tree; but if the abscess is great, and the fissures of the opening are many, then you should pause a hook in each piercing until they come together.
And if in the abscess there is a part of the membrane cut or hollowed out at its perimeter, then you should complete it with old linen or thread made of linen-yarn, as well as when you have extracted pus or roots, without moisture; and strengthen it on the third day; and then process it and heal it with that which one of the ointments within until it is healed.
But if blood occurs in the hour of your operation, then you should administer water mixed with vinegar in which one of linen is, and pause it upon the place of the flow of the blood many times.
But if the flow of blood persists, then you should administer regime and cure, and powders which I have recommended in many places of this book and of division.
But if it is in the time of winter, and the location of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you should mix powder with wine and oil, and pause them upon the locations.
And if it is in the summer, and the locations are muscular, then you should pause powders dampened with water and oil or wine and oil, and all of this should be rubbed until the third day as we have said, then you should dissolve the abscess and wash it and administer in its cure that which to it convenes until it is healed.
And this is that which is necessary of the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have said of every abscess in what manner is its way of cure by chapters singularly.
Chapter 41.
Of section of abscesses which occur in the membrane of the head.
In the membrane of the head there are small abscesses, and they are of species of nodes which contain membranes that are to them made; and their species is many.
And from them there are pustules, and from those one contains moisture similar to lime. And from those are ones that contain moisture similar to powder, and resembling it; and there are some that are scaly, hard.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of these there is not fear, as one must the extension of those does not contradict artery.
And the operation in section of these is that you express those with an instrument the form of which see there, the which is called entromes, so that you know that it contains.
For if that which is contained is moisture, then cut this with section according to length by superficial section according to this form:
And he begins at the section of the line of B. into the line of G. Therefore when the moisture is evacuated, then you scrape that which contains that moisture, and do not seek any cause from that, for many experienced physicians return, if something remains from that cause.
And then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment, if available, and if not, in water and salt; and fill it with that, and leave it until the next day, for with that you will dissolve all that is broken of that membrane.
And then apply Egyptian ointment a second and third time on the wound if you are confident that there is no cause from that membrane; then heal the wound with ointment until it is cured.
And if an abscess contains a hard nodule, then you cut into that according to this form: with a cross-shaped incision, and cut between the two lips of the incision and scrape that entirely out from the membrane that contains it, and exert your strength in extracting the lining which contains that.
But if your arrow causes you trouble, then do what I told you first.
And similarly do for an abscess which is suppurating with an incision and treatment as we have said before; and an incision on a suppurating abscess is easier, because it contains little pus and little moisture.
And sometimes there are some of these abscesses which are on the head in some people, for whom there is not any moisture; and the cause is that I incised an abscess on the head of an old woman and found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, which could not be broken up, and if someone hit it, it hurt.
But in the other abscesses which occur on the head, it is not like this, as with the abscesses which come to the heads of children and because of the roots of the ears; but the incision for these should be superficial.
And pause at the penetration of those in the lower part of them, so that the body is relieved from the sanies to the lower parts.
Then treat those with what is appropriate for that type of treatment.
Chapter .XLVII.
Of an incision on scrofula which occurs in the neck.
Often these abscesses occur in the neck and armpits and in the groin; and sometimes they occur in other parts of the body.
And those which occur in the neck, and many of them are engendered among themselves; and all scrofula of these is within its own membrane, and so with the nodules and abscesses of the head, as we have described.
And the species of these scrofula are many; for some are stony, and some contain moisture, and some are malignant and do not submit to treatment.
Therefore in that which you see with a good disposition in the touch, of which the color of what is seen is close to the color of the skin, and is swollen to all parts, and is not attached to the nerves of the neck, or the veins, or the artery, and is not deep, then you cut into that with a superficial incision from above to below the body along the line of G. into the line of B., and scrape that entirely out, and cut between its two lips with an incision, or with many incisions if you have need of those, as we said in the abscesses of the head; and extract that little by little.
And it is more cautious that the vein or nerve not be cut.
And be careful that the spatulum not strike suddenly, so that it does not hit your hand with an incision, or upset the patient, and cut into what is not necessary to be cut; for if you incised a vein or artery and prohibited yourself from your operation, then stop in the wound vinegar mixed with trass or other powders which stop the flow of blood, and close the wound, and leave it until that subsides the acuteness of the abscess, and becomes soft, and begins to become suppurating. When the blood is stopped.
Then return to your operation until you have finished.
Then inquire with your finger if any cause remains of the other little scrofula; then incise those and clean them.
And if there is a great vein in the root of the scrofula, then you should not incise that scrofula at its roots. But if you see that it falls by itself without harm, then leave that alone.
Then fill the wound with old ointment which you have already immersed in Egyptian ointment, and then heal that.
And if you incised that scrofula entirely, then you should attach the two lips of the wound and cauterize it so that no suppuration remains.
But if you see that there is suppuration because of the greatness of the scrofula, then you should understand how to incise its root, and drain that and administer a poultice and what is said.
And those of the scrofula which contain moisture, pierce that with a superficial incision where you see the place of its maturity to be, and pause an incision so that it drains the pus from below the body, as we have said.
Then administer an incision, poultices with ointment and similarly to those, so that it dissolves what is broken in the corrosion. Then when you see the wound already cleaned, then heal that with ointment of generative flesh until it is cured.
Chapter .XLVIII.
Of an incision on a boil which occurs in the gullet.
Others before us made this incision in the pilhot, and I have not seen anyone in our land who had that done.
And that is the inscription of their name.
But in men who have a hernia, then the extraction of the pilhot should be avoided, so that all the veins and the greater nerves of the patient are not cut.
But in those who have abscesses cauterized in the mouth or gullet or two ears, when the illness is not in the neck, then they should avoid an incision of the pilhot so that they avoid the danger which is done by penetration.
Then when we want that, let us incise the pilhot below three circles of the circles of the pilhot, or four with small incision for the width in that which is between two circles for quantity; and the incision should be in the pharynx, not in the cartilage, and that place is convenient for incision, because it is deprived of flesh, and the vessels of blood from him are long.
And if the patient is timid, then let the doctor stretch the gullet with an incision, and then cut the gullet so that it penetrates into the canal, but avoid the vessels of blood if he sees from those any cause.
Then incise the pharynx according to what we have recommended; and it is understood from the incision of the gullet by the flame which comes from him who is broken, and from the incision of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Then when the hour is swollen in which the penetration is seen, unite the two lips of the wound of the pharynx, and cut that only to the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that promote the growth of new flesh where it is needed.
And Al-Bukhari says that the meaning of this discourse which we have narrated is merely this: sometimes some of these abscesses have forced open the gullet of the patient; the patient has died, his bowels are protruded and some people cut into the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe on the spot where the plague is located and thus be saved from death.
And for this reason I command the opening of the pustule to be left open until the poison of the illness is expelled; and this poison lasts for three days; and then when the pustule is opened and treated in this manner, it will heal.
And what I have seen with my own eyes is that a servant held a pillow to his mouth and inserted the end of a pulmonary tube into his gullet; I was called to treat him, and when I discovered the pustule, I found blood coming out of it in small quantities.
And then he was made to confess that he had not punctured a vein or a nerve, and the wind escaped from the pustule and it healed.
And nothing happened to the servant unless he breathed through his mouth; then, after a few days, he returned to his usual condition.
And now I say that there is no fear in puncturing the epiglottis.
Chapter 44.
Of an incision on an abscess which occurs outside the gullet and is called a gullet hernia.
This hernia of the gullet is called a great abscess depending on the colour of the body, and it occurs in women.
And it happens in two ways: either naturally or accidentally.
And the natural one is incurable.
And the accidental one happens in two ways: the first is like fatty nodes and the other is like an abscess which occurs due to a knotted artery, and there is danger in that. And one should not make an incision on it with an iron instrument except in the case of a small one. And you should probe it and examine it with your finger; and if you find it like a fatty node and not attached to any vein, then you should open it in the same way as nodes, and extract all that the skin and bursa contain; otherwise, you should probe its whole substance, and treat the place with something suitable for healing until it is cured.
Chapter 45.
Of the sections of nodal tumours.
There are various kinds of nodes, and I have already described all their types in Division.
And what I will now account for is the difference between a node and an exit wound which causes doubt.
And I say that an exit wound is accompanied by heat, fever and violent pains until the ebullition of the superfluous matter ceases; and there is complete putrefaction when the fever, pain and heat subside.
But a node is not accompanied by heat, fever or pain; it contains its own sac.
And it depends on the colour of the body; its beginning is like a cyst and it occurs due to vacuousness, being either greater or lesser in size, and they are of two kinds: either fatty and containing moisture whose colours I have described in Division.
Therefore, when you come to treat a nodal tumour, you should probe it and examine its beginning with an instrument called an intrometer, depending on the form which will be described in the following chapter.
And this is the manner of examining an abscess and any node: you should take this instrument and insert it into the most moist part of the abscess which you find, and turn the instrument with a small movement until you know that it has penetrated the membrane.
Then stop your hand according to the size of the abscess, extract the instrument and consider what has come out through its orifice.
And if the moist matter has run out, regardless of its colour, then you should open it with a superficial incision as I have said in the case of other abscesses.
And if there is no moist matter coming out through the orifice of the instrument, then you should know that it is fatty.
And dry it with an incision having a cruciform shape according to this shape: cut it in this way and suspend it with hooks, and excise the membrane from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sac over it, if you can, and extract that pus from the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that pus; it happens many times that you should extract it little by little so that nothing remains inside which could cause any harm.
For if anything remains inside, a little or a lot, the node returns as before.
And if you see that a little remains inside, then complete the pustule with some caustic and corrosive powders, close the pustule and place your hand over it as before, and cure it by another method until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then cut its two lips and cure it with that which is encrusted.
But if the vein is pulsating or not, then cut and plug the place of the pulsatil vein which is opposite to it with a mixture of quicklime and vinegar and close that for two or three days until the pustule has suppurated and the effusion of blood has ceased; then return to opening what is broken in the node.

Chapter XLVII.
Of the cure of the breasts of men, which are like those of women.
Some men's breasts are swollen because of the act of sleeping with women, and then they become like women's breasts, swollen and pendulous.
And when you have done this, cut into those with a lunar incision according to this form, from the line of B to the line of G, and then remove the swollen flesh completely, and fill the wound with medicated ointment, and sew up the two lips of the wound, and cure that part which is healed.
But if the breast droops towards the armpit and is made soft by its weight, as in women, then it should be cut into two parts on either side with two incisions resembling a lunar figure, of which each part contains the other according to its end, so that the longer line contains the shorter according to this form, from the line of B to the line of G. And then remove the swollen flesh completely, and stitch up the lips of the wound, and administer what we have said about the sewing and the powders, which is necessary in the cure, until it is healed.
And if you do not complete the incision of that which must be cut for the inquietude of the patient and for the flow of blood, then fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment and leave that part until it is corroded by the ointment, and then cure that part which is healed.

Chapter XLIX.
Of the incision of abscesses which occur by artery or vein.
When an artery is broken and the vein is closed over it, then many times abscess occurs by artery or vein: for when the abscess is by artery it is long drawn out into the body; and when it is driven in by the veins, it feels in the place as a string does.
And that which is by vein is drawn around the surface of the body.
And the incision upon this abscess is error, and greater in that which is beneath the armpits, and in the angles, and on the neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is greater, therefore, when its cure with the iron is avoided, and that which is in the extremities, or on the head, let it be avoided.
But upon that which is of them by inflammation from the orifice of the artery, cut into the vein in its length; and then open the incision with pincers and then the artery, and free it from the tissues as far as it is uncovered.
Then place an needle on the spot and make it penetrate to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places — which causes you to lose your breath due to the constriction of two arteries located in the temples.
Then pierce the area between the two muscles with a spatulum so that all of the blood is drained from it and the boil is dissolved.
Then administer treatment to the area in which pus is formed so that the muscles are released from tension; and cure it with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
And if it is an apostema caused by a cut vein, then you must hold with your hand the area of the apostema with the thread, and insert the needle below the spot where your hand has been holding, and make it penetrate; and have a double thread inside so that you extract it from the other side, and bind the apostema with a good ligament according to what I told you in the ligament of grapes into two parts with two ends of the thread.
But if you are afraid of pulling out the thread, then insert the thread with that needle below all the apostema towards the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the apostema in the middle of it so that when it is dried out you insert the superfluity of the thread, and leave what is tied to it.
Then place on it a powder which you have soaked in wine and oil, and administer the treatment made with eggs and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 1 On the apostema which happens due to twisting of nerves.
As it happens with apostemas in arteries and veins, so apostemas happen in nerves when they experience impact or due to excess work and similarly.
And it is mostly formed in the places of the assistants or the ankle, or in any place where joints are injured.
And it is a serious apostema, and is similar in color to the rest of the body, and there are six symptoms of it when it is constricted with vehemence, and the patient experiences a stupor-like sensation.
And it is not an apostema located in the abdomen, and for that reason it has no thread, and it is injured on every side, and does not go to the sides in front or behind.
Therefore for those who have apostemas in their joints do not need to be bound with iron, because they will experience contraction very quickly.
But for the one who has it on the head or forehead, cut the thread with a spatulum. But if it is a small apostema, then grab it with tweezers and pull it out by its roots.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and cut it open, and draw it out; and stitch the wound closed, and cure it until it heals.
Chapter .ii.
On the section of apostema which happens due to chyle that happens in the abdomen.
This happens to some men a few times in their bellies and in the other parts of their bodies, those whose heads are small and the rest of them are like mushrooms due to similarity to mushrooms, whose roots are thin but their caps are large; and already their lips are twisted, and they are either very petite or highly magnified.
And I have indeed seen one such person, and in his belly there were two things which looked like mushrooms, and there was no difference between them and white ones, with thin roots.
And already their lips were reversed and splitting, and humidity flowed from them all the time.
Therefore I opened them up and found in one of them 15 small stones. And the other six inches.
And the operation at the incision of them is that you consider whether the patient is cold, and if the color of the wound is white, then you open it with a spatulum from the side, and let it be cauterized in the fire, because many times after the section some blood is expelled; and if you stop the blood, cauterize it.
And if you see the patient is fearful and anxious, be cautious about making an incision with iron; but take recent lead thread and tighten it on the wound, in the manner which we have described earlier; and leave it for two days.
Then adjust in the tightening of the lead thread; therefore, do not stop from tightening the large thread greatly on the wound until it is cut off and falls by itself.
But if the wound is of thick roots, then in its incision there is a cause for fear and terror, especially that which is in the abdomen.
But it is possible for you to split the majority of it, and then cauterize it so that it does not return.
Then cure it until the wound is healed.
And beware that you do not assume to incision a wound which is of dusky color, of little feeling, of weak pulse, because this one is certainly cancerous.
And I come with the memory of knowledge.
Chapter .ii.
On the treatment of an outstanding umbilicus.
Eminence of the umbilicus is caused by many reasons; or by fissures of the liver which is over the abdomen, and from it the membrane or intestine according to where other ruptures are; or by blood which flows from a vein or artery as mentioned earlier, or by constricted vasoconstriction in it.
But if it is by fissure of the liver and thickening of the membrane, then the color of the apostema is similar to that of the body; and it has little pain, and appears in various locations. And if it is by prolapse of the intestine, then its location is as we have mentioned earlier, with more violent diversity, and when you push it in with your fingers it conceals itself, and then returns; and quickly it becomes large, and is magnified much due to bathing and violent work.
But if it is by humidity, then it is easy and does not conceal itself when you push with your hand, nor is it constricted nor burned.
And if it is by blood, then with these signs the apostema turns black and declines.
But if it is by pus, then it is a serious apostema, large and hard, and is formed according to an amount.
But if it is by vasoconstriction, then the touch of it is tender.
And the operation on it is that you consider whether the eminence of the umbilicus is by blood of an artery or vein, or by vasoconstriction; then beware of treating it because in that there is fear and terror as I instructed in the chapter about apostemas by artery and vein.
And if the eminence of the umbilicus is by the intestine or membrane, then command the patient to hold his navel, and let him stand extended; then feel with your fingers all around the umbilicus, and then command him to bend towards you between your hands over his navel, and let him circle it with a spatulum from the side where you have felt with your fingers; then extend the majority of the apostema to the sides above it with a large hook; and tie in the circuit with strong thread or with twine in the decent manner.
Then open the middle of the extended apostema over the intestine and insert your finger into that hollow and if you have tied it nor guarded by the intestine, then extract the herniated and push the intestine to the sides inside the abdomen.
And if you have found the hernia, then take it in your hand; and squeeze out the superfluities from it.
But if it is contrary to your archery or vein, then surround that spot, and return to your operation; and take two needles and put them into those two warts very firmly, and pierce through the wart in a cross shape, making sure the needles penetrate; and tightly grab the wart in four places on the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and let the flesh extend and fall back by itself; or squeeze out what is being thinned and let it heal with ointment covering the wound so that it may be healed.
And if the protuberance of the navel is filled with flesh or by humidity, then you must hollow out the hernia as we have said and squeeze out the blood or humidity which you find there, and then cure it with ointment covering the wound so that it may be healed and consolidated.
Chapter 53:
Of the cure for a hernia.
We have already said, in the division, about the kind of hernia and how it is cured by medicines, and that it is cured with iron without being ulcerated; and we have also mentioned the generation of a hernia, as well as the caution regarding its cure.
And the ancients said that sometimes a hernia is found in places where its removal is possible, such as in the breast or in the groin and similar places in other parts of the body; they advised to extract all of it, especially when it is starting out small.
But when it is old and large, do not attempt to remove it, for I have never seen one healed by this method nor have I heard of it happening.
And the operation on it, when it is located as we have said, is that you precede and let the patient fast and purge of black bile, and then bleeding is done if a manifest fullness is found.
Then prepare the patient with a preparation in which he is placed for the operation, and then pierce him with hooks that reach into the hernia; and concavely, all around with a good sharp knife, examine thoroughly so that no cause of the hernia remains. Let the blood flow, and do not quickly cut it off; squeeze out the places and wipe away the clotted blood with your hand or with an instrument through which you can easily reach.
But if you find that there is an obstruction of blood from a vein or artery, then cauterize it so that the flow of blood ceases, and then cure it with the other cure so that it may be healed.
Chapter 54:
Of the cure for hydrocephalus.
We have already recommended in the division about the kinds of hydrocephalus from water, and the signs of each kind, as well as the cure for it with medicines.
And that which is cured by iron is only the kind called 'althitas', and it should not be approached with iron as regards the kind of 'timpanistres' nor the kind of 'ypotarcha', for both are mortal.
And when you have medicated this kind of hydrocephalus timpanistre with medicines and it does not respond to your treatment, then consider, for if the patient already has debility or another malady such as another hydrocephalus, just as if there is a cough or intestinal illness and similar to these, then be wary and do not treat it with iron, for fear of this.
But if you see the patient suffering from abundant vertigo and there is no other malady in him except hydrocephalus, and he is not a child nor old, then the manner of operating on him is to elevate the patient between your hands, and the minister should then squeeze his belly with his hand, filling the water up into the part below the navel, and then take a pointed spatula according to this form:
It should be in two pointed parts, with a pointed end just like the spatula; but indeed it should be a little shorter in length so that during the operation you do not pass into the intestine, and then lead him.
Then consider if the generation of hydrocephalus is from parts of the intestines, for then you should lengthen him with the incision from the navel by the amount of three digits below, in his right side over the navel.
But if the generation of hydrocephalus is due to illness of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the navel by three digits.
And if its generation is due to a cold, then your incision should be on his right.
And do not let your incision be over the side on which the patient wants to lie so that the superfluities do not flow into that place.
Then pierce with the instrument all around, and insert into that incision, and elevate your hand with the spatula between the membrane and the brain, and you should draw it out; and if it is the amount of a nail or so much.
Then pierce the brain so that the spatula reaches the desired place, which is where the water is. Then extract it and insert an instrument of which this is the form: which is like a slender silver tube; it is made of silver or brass or lead; and in the lowest part of it there is a small incision, and on its sides there are three incisions: two from one side and one from the other side; and its end is split according to the manner of a feather, just like this:
And in the highest end of it is a ring, for when the instrument reaches the water, then that immediately slips over the instrument, thus evacuating the water in the momentary quantity; for if you evacuate more than this, then the patient dies from resolution of his animal spirit, or he experiences an attack which is close to death.
But you should evacuate it according to the quantity of the vertigo and according to what the dispositions of the patient's vertigo, his pulse and health indicate to you.
Then extract the instrument and pour out the water which is causing it, for as soon as you have extracted the instrument, it will pour out just like the water.
Then return the instrument on another day if you see the patient tolerating it, and extract a little water, and do this for several days out of fear, and beware of mistakes so that the water does not remain except a little.
But if you fear for the patient and pour out a great quantity of water, then cure him with a burial in dry sand, and move him to the bath, and let him stay in the sun for a long time; and cure him with drying medicines so that he may be healed.
And cauterize over the stomach, and the liver and gallbladder, and especially the extraction of the water, according to what I have recounted before.

Chapter 65.
On the treatment of intestinal hernia.
The occurrence of this hernia is due to a rupture that extends into the chest from the anus of the rectum, so that as a result of this rupture some of the intestines pass out through the opening.

And the cure of it is with cautery as it is preceded by the narration of it.

And then strengthen the white diaphragm which is under the scrotum so that it is uncovered.
And then take the needle and apply it to the protruding place of the chest, and press it against the abdomen.
Then cut the two prominent spots on top of the head's crown, and sew one to the other.
Then pull out the end of the bone, and don't cut into the skull at all, nor stretch the nerve, or any other cause as well, as you will learn in the treatment of intestinal hernias.
And then cure that with the treatment of ulcers, and when you insert the needles, cleanse it and restore the ulcer within so that it is consolidated; for the skull is contracted and not adjusted to the突出 of the rupture.
And cautery is better in this place, because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68:
Of the softening of the cords of the testicles.
Many times the cords of the testicles in some men are softened because the flesh that is between them is softened, and the guarding of it is relaxed.
Then it is necessary for the one who is being treated to lie on his back, and to heat all the cords which are softened over the natural cords; then sew two lips together.
And if you want, cut in the beginning of the surplus of the softened cord with three cuts or four and with a firm suture.
And then insert between the sutures, and cure through the treatment of other ulcers within so that it is healed and the needles fall out.
Chapter 69:
Of castration:
You should know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but for two reasons I have been asked to include it in this book; one of which is so that the doctor who is questioned about it knows how to cure it if it happens, and the other reason is that many times we need to castrate other animals for our own purposes, like mules, oxen, pigs, and similar beasts.
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting through to a section.
But in the one that is done by crushing, the way of the operation is to have the beast cut into cold water until its testicles are softened and loose and hanging. And then take those with your hand so that they are dissolved and do not appear below the touch.
But in castration done by cutting through, catch hold of the beast and press the cords of its testicles with your left hand.
And then cut the suspenders, and insert into each one a section so that two holes are made.
And then insert those after you have scraped off each one. And do not put anything on the skull over them except for the thin skull which is above the vessels.
And this way of castration is better which is done by crushing, because crushing strongly leaves no cause in the testicles so that the beast desires coitus.
And then cure the ulcer within until it is healed.
Chapter 70:
Of the cure of hermaphrodites:
Hermaphrodites in men are according to two ways: one is when they appear to have a space between the cords of the testicles, in that which is between the two testicles there is a figure like a woman’s vulva in which there are hairs.
And sometimes from it urine flows from that which is in the cords of the testicles.
But in women there is one type: and it is that the clitoris of a woman on the foreskin is like two testicles of a man, a little bit of all of them at the beginning of the penis, just like the foreskin of a man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three types: two from men and one type from women. And it is so that you insert those flesh parts joined together so that the impression of them flows out, and then cure those with the treatment of other ulcers.
And in the second type from men from which urine flows and which is in the cords of the testicles, there is no cure or operation for it.
Chapter 71:
Of the hymen and prominent flesh from causes in women:
A strong hymen is firmly attached to natural causes so that it is strained and made tight by the guarding; and sometimes it is enlarged in some women as much as in men, and it comes into coitus.
So then take hold of the surplus of the hymen with your hand or a needle and insert.
And do not pierce all the way through, especially in the root of the vein, so that it does not draw out blood.
And then cure it with the treatment of other ulcers within until it is healed.
But a born flesh is flesh which grows in the womb of the mother so that it fills that place, and often it comes out at the openings in front according to the appearance of the vagina (and for this reason some first called it “tail with a head”); therefore we insert as we insert the hymen, and cure it within until it is healed.
Chapter 72:
Of the cure of anus.
Anus is when the clitoris of a woman is not perforated, or has a small hole. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is by disease which has preceded it, and that one is done, or by flesh grown together, or by a thin skull, or hard.
And it is done, or in the root of the mother, or in its sides, or on top of it, or on the bottom of it, and very much prohibits coitus and impregnation, and very much prohibits menstruation.
And the knowledge of it is done by guarding of the midwife, if the swelling is apparent, the midwife; but if it is not apparent, then you probe it with your fingers or with a needle.
But if the swelling is by a thin skull and is against the two lips, then you cut and tear it apart.
And it is that you pause over the two lips of the vagina, and then pause your fingers indicating both sides from within.
And the woman be on her back, her legs spread out, and then extend the two lips with force within so that that thin skull is broken and the swelling opened.
And then take wool and dip it in oil and pause it over the place, and put on a poultice at night so that the place is not healed up.
But if the skull is thick and hard, then take that with fat of lard or pitch of myrrh.
But if the swelling is by flesh grown together, then suspend it with a needle, and insert it.
And have you the medicines that make the flow of blood stop, like a biting wound, and dragon’s blood, and gum arabic, tied up with white of egg.
And then administer a broad lead cane so that the wound is not healed tightly.
And hold it for several days, and give warm water of linseed.
And then it is healed by the other cure of consolidation within until it is healed.
And sometimes others happen in the womb of mothers, and then take hold of them according to this way. But if it is due to scrofulous sores, do not cause any contraindications with iron in any way for the scrofulous sores that are on the neck.
Chapter 73.
Of the cure for hemorrhoids, and of a tail and red spot that occurs in the genitals of women.

Chapter 74.
Of boring a hole in the anus accidentally.

Chapter 75.
To teach the midwives in what manner the child is to be treated when it appears according to an unnatural figure.
It is necessary that the midwife know in the beginning the figure of the childbirth by its signs and when you see the woman expressing on the parts below and desiring to smell the air, and upon it she is raised because of what is above her, and hastens the delivery of the child; then know that this part is according to a natural figure, and the delivery of it is over her head, and the second one with it or suspended from or hanging from the umbilical.
Therefore when you see these signs, then let the belly of it be pressed so that the embryo descends gently when she descends over her head; let the second one descend with it or hang from the umbilical.
But he who is in this part is unnatural and not possible; when the child is ejected over his feet and the body of him is ejected before his head and his feet, or under his armpit. or the head of him is ejected and his hand or to his belly, and he is turned strong on his neck; and like the figures of him are not possible.
It is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all these causes, and that she keep from error and deception.
And I will show you all the figures of them and what cunning is in them so that it be signified by that and is placed upon that.
When the child is ejected upon his head by natural violence, and it is violent over the woman and its part is difficult, and see that the strength of him is already weakened, then let her sit, or that women hold him; and evaporate the womb of him with fenugreek coarsely ground and with oiled herbs.
And if the midwife inserts between his buttocks a little spatula and widens with it the second one, or cuts that with her finger until she touches what is in her of moisture. And press on the abdomen of the woman until you feel the fetus descend.
But if she does not deliver, then it is necessary that the woman be cleansed with poultices of fennel and fenugreek with honey.
Then command him, the provider of the treatment, to make her vomit and cause her to sneeze with that mixture; and hold her mouth and nose for an hour so that the fetus will come out immediately.
And if both hands of the fetus are not exposed at first, then it is necessary to pull them out little by little with ease. But if she does not react to the remedy, then put her on a bed and raise her feet up, and rock the bed back and forth gently on the ground; and make sure that the woman does not fall off the bed because of the rocking.
And if the hands are not turned inside out and the fetus is still dead, then enter them again and draw out the fetus's limb or tie the body to your hand with a cloth and pull it out evenly, for that will come out.
When the fetus is on his feet, then it is necessary to push them up, and gently turn the fetus, and make him cough, and grab one of his feet and stretch them little by little.
But when it has entered the pelvis, then command him to push, and make her vomit with that mixture, for it will come out if God wills it.
And if it is not delivered with what we have described, then return the fetus little by little to where you found it, and place that second figure naturally, for it will come out more easily the second time.
And if all that we have described is prohibited, then take fennel and dissolved gum in the mortar and beat them well together, and line the vagina of the woman with it, at the bottom of her abdomen. And make her sneeze in warm water until she expels the phlegm.
And when the parts below him are softened, then make smoke of myrtle and place that under him. And when she has been in the smoke for an hour, then make her sneeze on a bed and cause her to cough and draw out her mouth, and press the lower part of her abdomen gently, for the fetus will come out immediately.
Descent of the fetus hanging down from one of its hands. Let him be drawn in to reduce the hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and make her walk.
And if she cannot walk, then make her lie on a cloth and rock her thighs violently with strong concussion, and administer to her soothing remedies which are made from mucilaginous substances.
And if the labor has come, then make her sneeze on a bed, and study the reduction of the hand, and gently turn the fetus according to its natural figure, and make the woman cough and command him to push himself while it is delivered.
Descent of the fetus on his neck with his arms expanded and his chest against his mother's back. Let the midwife hold the fetus's hand, and then roll it little by little, and let that be done with ease.
And when he is and as soon as he is bathed, then put on him what we have described of oil and mucilaginous substances.
Then command him to suck little by little, and when you have done that, then make her sneeze on a bed and command him to be inclined on the right side, and then command her to push; and make her cough with that mixture. Exit of the fetus prepared on its side.
When it comes out of the mother's womb in this way, consider and then enter the second one with your finger so that the moisture is evacuated.
And if the fetus is suspended over his face and neck, then enter that with your finger so that it is not retained and delayed.
Then press the fetus to the inside parts so that it is not retained and delayed; and command the woman to push several times, and he will come out with easy exit if God wills it.
Exit of twins or many fetuses. Know that many times twins are born, and sometimes one or two or three or four, but that is strange and rare; but its cause is natural, and they do not live.
Count them, even if they are doubled, a second one, and they are separated by the umbilical cord, distinguish those enter the ligament in the navel of each of them; and sometimes they are delivered so easily as is one fetus with easy exit, and sometimes they are delivered so that we have described.
And if they are difficult to deliver and come to that which we have said of the non-natural figures, then you treat them as we have recorded.
And if the midwife is skillful and does that with ease and skill, and there is delay, let her be treated according to the whole figure as it is prepared by the medicine bringing health.

Of the forms of the instruments which are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of vertigine with which is open the vagina:
This is the form of stricture in which are closed the lips, to that closure are two virtues in two ends of two roots. But this virtue let it be more subtle of stricture, and let it be made either of ebony or of boxwood.
And let the thickness of each wood be two fingers and the edge of either two fingers or one finger, and the length of each is one palm and a little more; and in the middle place of the two woods are two joints of that woods which are already closed, of which the length is the measure of one palm and a little more, and the thickness of each is two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the vagina so that it is open with those when you turn about the two prescribed vertigines.
Other form also similar to that more subtle and more distant:
Let it be made of boxwood or of ebony according to the likeness of forceps. However, at the end of his body there are two additions, and the length of those additions is one palm each, and the width of each is two digits.

Of extraction of the second child:
When the second child is retained by childbirth, then you must command the patient to retain their breath, and then make them sneeze with snuff, and stretch your hand over their mouth and nose, and if it comes out with that, it's good.
And if not, then you take a woollen ball and pierce the cloth with a needle and soak that in herbs that open the mouth of the vagina, like hellebore and rue and anise and chamomile and Arabic scilla and cinnamon and frankincense. All of these herbs or some of them are soaked in water in the ball, and place that on the fire.
Then place a straw in the mouth of the vagina, and keep that there until the vapor comes to the cavity of the vagina.
And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the second child will be pushed out with speed.
But if this treatment has not worked and it hasn't come out, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in olive oil or in mustard of alder, and then insert that in the vagina and feel for the second child with that, and when she has found it, take it and stretch it little by little according to rectitude so that the mother doesn't cry out because of the strong pulling. Before that is done, let it be turned to the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the vagina is constricted, we have already recommended the treatment with sneezing and with medication of the ball with herbs.
But if it has not been pushed out with all the causes that we have recommended, then be careful not to tire her with iteration of pulling, but instead let what comes out of her mouth at the vagina lie on the woman' couch; and then let that be sealed with ointment and tetrafarmacon, because that will make it putrefy in a few days and dissolve and be pushed out.
But when it rises, there is a bad smell to the head and stomach, and that makes the patient sick; therefore let balms be administered below the smoke and convenient things to that.
But some of the Ancients have been tested with smoke of nettle and dry figs.
The shape of the instrument by which the woman is smoked because of retention of menstruation and of the second child:
It is made of glass or of horn.
