Of incision extremities and of the jointing of bones.
The extremities may be affected either by an intrinsic or extrinsic cause, or as you have medicated that corruption for the sake of cure with those medicines and the cure does not confer, or else the corruption goes away from the member in which case you did not perceive any cause, then when you insert that member into that place where the corruption used to be, so that the patient escapes from death or from some greater harm to the member.
And the sign of that to which it happens is that the member becomes black as if it had been burned, or it may happen near the blackness that that corruption entered into that member and spread throughout the entire body; and then cut off with an incision at that place.
And similarly if the cause of the corruption is a poisonous strike from some venomous creature like that of the sea scorpion or of the viper or of the adder or of their likes.
And if the corruption or strike is on the extremity of the finger, then you shall insert the finger and not give space to the corruption so that it enters into the hand.
And similarly if it happens to the hand, then you shall insert it at the joint of the arm, and not give space to the corruption so that it enters into the arm.
And if instead it is the other one, then insert the arm within the elbow at the joint.
And if the corruption passes further and goes around the elbow, then in that is the death of the patient; and to impart another cause for cure in addition to this is a quantity of virtue.
And similarly do the foot when corruption happens to the toe, then you shall insert that within one of the toes.
And if it affects the heel of the foot, then you shall insert all of the foot. But if it enters into the toe, then you shall insert the instep at the joint of the toe.
And if the corruption is already past onto the toe, then in it there is not healing but dismissal, and let the patient go to his death.
And the manner of inserting the member or of cutting it is that you tighten the ligament at the part which is lowest and which you want to insert, and tighten another ligament over the place; and extend the minister one ligament to the parts below, and extend the other minister over it; and you separate the flesh which is between two ligaments as far down as possible so that all the flesh is uncovered; and then let it be cut or cut into.
And so that a bandage of linen is placed over all the parts so that it does not touch the wound, and that the patient come healed and bound up.
But if it happens bleeding of blood when they are opened, then you cauterize the place burnt-wise, or pause over there some powders that constrict the bleeding; and then return to your medicine until it is complete.
And then bind the member bandaged with a ligament in a convenient way, and cure that until it is healed.
And I return to you that which happened to a man on his foot, this wound which accident I and you recommended, which is when he became blackened on his foot by scorching that was like the burning of fire.
And that corruption happened first on his toe before it extended over all the foot.
And then that man prepared for himself remedies more than once that the cure might go to the member with the force of it, and he struck that foot until it hurt and burned, and he cauterized that foot at the joint, and healed it with fire.
Long time ago that corruption happened on the toe of the hand as mentioned.
And then it went to me, and so I perceived that superfluity with that which was paused over the hand of the remedies, then the cleansing of its body; and the superfluity is not repelled and began going to the other toe before it began in the hand.
And he led me to insert the hand into it, and I did not want to expect anything about the result of that superfluity, and yet that I feared would be the death of the patient if the virtue of the medicine was over powerful.
And since he left me it returned to his land and it was perceived that that man prepared and inserted his entire hand, and it healed.
And I have not added this narration except that it be aid to what is added to this illness, and that it be significance by which it was signified and according to which it was turned.
Of cure of sores and quality of cauterization with medicines.
When it happens to apostema on some members of the flesh and the space of the apostema is prolonged so that there is collection of pus, and then it is broken and perforated, and the pus comes out from it, and the wound is cleansed as if it were washed, and the stringy part which is above it as if it were a veil, and it does not come to a deeper corruption, and not impresses into the bone or on the nerves or on the ligaments, it is called sinus, and it is not named fistula.
But if the space is prolonged so that the corruption infects in some member, then it is called sinus and not fistula.
And the cure of it is that you insert that stringy part all around as it is unwound, and more so when it is cut with a razor, and compressions are made so that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
But if you expect that the stringy part adheres and that corruption has not happened because of deeper cauterization, and in the stringy part there is swelling from the face, then you cure that by cautery.
Consider the armpit, and if it is large, and the arm that you see has an offensive odor, then cleanse that with Egyptian medicine which is made of oil and wine, mixed with rosemary, received in equal parts, and placed in a vessel, and cooked over fire until the medicine becomes hot and reaches the consistency of honey.
Then take from him what is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and cleanse the armpit with that medicine, and strengthen the opening of it, and leave the medicine in there for the amount of two hours.
Then remove that with a sponge; and do this for so many days until the armpit is cleansed and the odor is removed.
And sometimes it is cleansed with water of ashes when that medicine is not present to you; and take the ashes of wood and place water on it, and then boil that and cleanse the armpit with it until you are certain that the armpit is cleaned.
And if the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then cleanse that with water and honey in which is mixed ground rosemary, and also cleanse it with wine and honey mixed, for the property of honey is to clean and wash, and the wine causes adhesion of the armpit, and especially when there is excess of dryness and tightness in the wine.
And when you do this some times and are convinced that the armpit is cleaned, then cleanse that with water that causes the flesh to grow in it.
And take a thin ointment and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine, or cleanse that with some medicines and other ointments that have the properties which I have already written about in the treatise on ointments.
And if the opening of the armpit is narrow and does not receive the catheter of the clyster, then expand that little by little with a small iron rod and place a heated sponge wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment on it until it is expanded.
And similarly if the opening is wide, then sew up its edges and leave in it a quantity that the clyster can enter without addition.
And if the opening of the armpit from which the arm hangs is elevated to the parts above it, then dry that in the place that is below for the arm to hang down into it, for when the arm is constricted in the depth of the armpit flesh is generated in it.
And if it is not possible for you to dry the armpit within the bone below according to what you want, then it is necessary that you prepare the member with preparation so that the arm runs from it slightly according to what seems appropriate to you and that no cause of the arm be retained in it.
But that which is over the opening of the armpit, and cleansed at every hour so that what is inserted in it of the arm dries. And so that you know if what runs from it of the arm is little or much, or is digested, or not digested.
And with this you consider the place of that armpit, if in it the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an ulcer in it.
And when your medicine is prolonged in such a manner and you see the matter that is formed over the opening of the armpit already dry or having dried up, then loosen it on the third day, and when you loosen the plaster, then change the cloth for another and renew the ointment.
But if from the armpit a subtle virus is seen to run long spaces, then do not despair of its adhesion for it, for its healing is proper, for some men in whom generation of flesh in their plasters is slow, and of those so whose contrary is done.
And if from the armpit after many days an indigest arm is issued, then know that the armpit does not adhere; and if adhesion of the armpit is delayed and the cause prolonged, then you reduce in dryness of the medicines, and if the medicines are moist in their substance and in their power, they are dried as with thin ointment when there is in it excess of addition of wax.
And the last with which it is cured, is that you take thin ointment and dissolve it in rose oil, and over it pour old wine equal in its substance, and then be convinced of that, and use it.
And then do likewise in that action when there is no arm, take thin ointment and honey when it is cooked until it is thickened, and use it; or take myrrh and aloe and aloes wood, and grind all and pulverize over the honey when it is over fire, and then line that over cloth and strengthen it over the armpit; and line that with the honey which you have cooked until it is thickened, and pulverize over cloth and strengthen that.
And sometimes they are administered to it with long aristology and radishes of celestial lily (and is celestial lily) and farina of oats and centaurea, and use of those simples or adjusted, grind all and sift over the honey which you have recommended; and use it.
And if the armpit is prolonged and is not healed by this treatment, then know that corruption is in its depth, and then make incision into the bones or in the other hard members or the ligaments; then you cure it with tubular treatment as above is said.
Of treatment of ulcer and nail worn down and addition of finger cut and section.
Ulcer is an ulcer which arises below the nail of the finger on the hand or foot, and strongly affects the other fingers and when it is prolonged and its healing is long delayed, or is an ulcer of an ulcerous wound, or is corrupted, and issues arm within that corrodes the radicle of the nail, and strongly corrupts all that, and strongly permeates to the bone within which there is an offensive odor, and its end is made black.
And so when you have that with what we have said in the division and do not confer your treatment then know that you cut out all the excess which is rotted from the nail and then cauterize the wound therefore, for cautery of motion is beneficial in this.
But if the bone is whole and the nail is healed, and the additions of the nail become compact, and begin to prick and stab that, then know that you place fine thread below the edge of the nail which pricks the flesh, and drive that up and insert that flesh with ease, and place over that which comes from the flesh of scorching medicines within until it is all cleansed; and then cure that with ointments so that it is healed.
But if the corruption is already in the bone, then you must cut into that bone and extract it, for there is no hope of healing as long as the bone remains corrupted.
And if you see corrosion and corruption in the finger, then cut into it at one of its joints according to how you remember it, and dress the wound so that it may heal.
But if there is a blow or injury to the fingernail, and consequently great pain in it, then at the beginning you must bleed the patient, and then dry the nail with a sharp spatula by making a transverse cut across it, being careful that the cut does not extend into the flesh below the nail, for you will cause great pain to the patient, and will prevent the superfluous flesh from growing back in that place; and dress the wound to ease the pain.
But this tissue, which is born in the hands of some men, has very little flesh and very few bones, or very little nail.
And some are born in the web of the joint, or their origin is in some joints of the fingers. But that which is born in some joints of the finger does not harm, and that which is born in the joints is very harmful.
And with those that are born fleshy, the cut is easier, and you must cut into it at its root with a broad spatula.
But that which is born in the root of the joint, its treatment is difficult; and so beware of cutting it off.
But in that which is born on a finger at the joint, you must cut into the flesh of it with a round incision into the bone, and then cut with one of those appropriate saws for this purpose, and dress the wound so that it may heal.
But consolidation which happens to the fingers among their joints, either by habit of the person who was born like that, or by consolidation of a plague, or by burning with fire, or by similar means, then you must dry up that consolidation so that the fingers return to their natural shape.
And then place between them pieces of linen soaked in rose oil so that they are not consolidated quickly, and separate those pieces, or place between them a thin sheet of lead so that it is consolidated according to how you wish.
And likewise if consolidation happens in some fingers with the palm, then you must dry up that consolidation according to how it is prepared and convenient for the figure of the member.
Of incisions of veins, thus are varicose.
Varicose veins and grossly swollen full of melancholy superfluities which come in parts of the body, and their greatest occurrence is in the legs, and most commonly in the legs of travellers and labourers and carriers.
Then you must administer purgation of the body from black bile several times with strong expulsion, and then bleed the patient from the basilic vein.
But their treatment with iron is according to two methods: the one is that it is cut and that black blood is drawn, and the other method is that the vein is elevated and all of it is extracted.
The cutting of it is according to this method: at the beginning moisten the leg with warm water so that the gross blood which is feculent from the leg is resolved, and then tightly press the leg of the patient at the part above the highest part of the thigh into the part below the groin with a bandage, and then dry up the vein in one place or two or three with a broad cut, and then elevate the black blood by your hand from the part below the leg upwards into itself, and from there downwards, so that the amount which you wish to and can bear is expelled, and which the strength of the patient permits.
And then ligate it, and command him to abstain from foods engendering black bile.
And repeat the treatment by phlebotomy when the veins are full and this is noticed by the patient.
But the elevation of them is according to this method: you raise the leg of the patient if there are pains in it, and then place him in a bath and moisten his leg with warm water so that it swells up and the veins are expanded; or let him be exercised by vigorous exercise, if a bath is not available, so that the member is warmed.
And then dry up the vein on the right side of it by a cut in its length or in its thickness, or at the bottom of it above the ankle.
And then open up the vein with nails and gouge out the vein from every part so that it appears to him, and you must examine it so that he perceives that darkness is inclining towards blackness.
And therefore when you open up and draw out from the vein, then you will see that it is white like a chord.
And then you must place below it the ray so that it is elevated and let blood out of the vein, and suspend it with a lion's tooth.
And then make another cut just above that cut for three fingers, and gouge out the vein from the part above the vein so that it appears.
And then elevate it and cut into it in the back just above the ankle, and then extract that and elevate it so that it is expelled by the second cut, and then extract it from the cut which is above that.
And do this so that you extract it from the cut which is highest or highest of all the cuts, so that all of it is expelled; and then cut into it.
And if he does not obey you to be extracted and elevated, then insert a strong bent needle into it and tie it up and extract it, or insert below it the ray and revolve your hand all around so that it is expelled. And beware of cutting it; for if it is broken, it is made difficult for you to elevate that part and it has come upon the patient through that harm.
And when all of it has been expelled, then place over the part of the plague wool soaked in wine and rose oil and not-rose oil, and dress that so that it may heal.
And if the part is contracted having tortuousness to which there is envelopment in its parts, and it is not according to rectitude as we have said, then you must split that at every part of tortuosity of it and at places of envelopment of it, and then suspend that with nails so that you elevate it all.
And beware of your cutting that you do not cut the vein and that you do not plague it, for it will be difficult for you to elevate it; and exercise your prudence in it.
Form of the incision by which it is dried out:
It is not to be used in this way with nails nor is it of acute extremity so that it does not plague the vein; and it is of gross flexibility, for if it were subtle, it would cut into the vein through its subtlety; there are in it superfluous thicknesses, as we have said.
Of extraction of vein of leg:
This vein is engendered in the legs in warm lands like Atak in the land of Arabs and in warm and arid lands of little tenderness, and in those where there is no grass or tree.
And it is very rarely engendered in other parts of the body besides the legs.
And its gestation is of putrefaction which comes from below the vein like venom inside the body of serpents and worms and scars and worms engendered between the vein and flesh.
And the sign of the occurrence of this disease is that a violent inflammation occurs in the leg, and the site becomes blistered; and then the vein begins to flow from the site of that blister, which looks like it has been burned by a plant.
And then when his feet appear, you should wrap around them a piece of lead weighing two drachms, and tie it and let the lead hang from his leg.
And as many times as you see something coming out of it from outside, wrap that in lead and cut it. And if it is prolonged, then you insert a piece of it and wrap the rest; but do not insert the part that has been cut off, because when it is inserted it contracts and goes into the flesh causing an abscess and pus in the site and a bad ulcer.
So it should be treated gently and extracted little by little, while being pushed out from the back of it, so that it does not pull anything else into the body.
And from this vein some people have had it coming out to be the length of 5 or 10 palms, and I myself have seen one that was 20 palms long.
And if it is cut in the time of its treatment, then you insert a needle into the hole of it and perforate it with a long needle into the body, so that everything that is in the matter is evacuated, and bring about putrefaction of the site for several days with medicines; and then cure it by the cure for abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has bumps, and mostly when it appears at the junction of the leg or in the leg, and there come to it many openings, and it flows from every opening like a ram.
And so you cure that as we have said above, and with what is said above.
Of the cutting of worms generated under the skin and it is called the sickness of cattle.
This disease is called in some lands by the name of "bovine disease" because many times it affects oxen and it is a worm that is born between the skin and the flesh, and goes through all the body pushing and falling, and is made manifest to the sense by moving from one member to another until it breaks the skin and comes out.
And its generation is by putrefaction of some humor so that worms and serpents and roundworms and ascariasis occur in the belly.
And it is feared for its malice, because when it goes into the body and is elevated to the head, and it reaches the heart, then it suddenly pierces in there and destroys the heart, and from there many times.
And so when you want to cure that and extract it, then do not do it unless by the movement of it and its appearance to the sense, and then you tightly press what is above it and what is below it with strong constriction, and then dry over it and extract it.
And if it is hidden in the flesh and you do not touch it, then you put cautery with fire over the site where it resides, and the greater cause that is feared is corruption of it by which the site is corrupted as we have said.
But if you see it having reached the head close to the heart, then press tightly over the forehead with a strong constriction, and then dry over it, and extract it; and let the patient use purification of his body with medicaments that evacuate bad putrid humors, and guard against foods that generate putrefaction.
Of the cutting of the sickness of children.
This disease is called in our land "nafir", and it is a pain that comes in some members, and then it is moved from member to member.
And I have seen it according to what you will tell me. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and I discovered her arm and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm, and pus that had come out for an hour, I saw that inflammation going like a worm pushing from one site to another, but more quickly than it could move, like silver when it is drawn from one place to another.
And then it went into the pain of that site and pierced the muscle, and then it stuck there for a while.
And then it went into the other arm as far as the other leg.
And then I saw it revolving throughout his body according to what I saw; and it was too marvelous of the change of it and its speed from member to member. And I had already seen this before in my eyes according to that manner, but I have seen many which carry the pain being moved from member to member. But I did not see it with the arms as with the woman.
And I did not think it was that unless that the woman was of old age, one of whose body and veins were withered away, and in which appeared to the sense that winding movement.
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this back-cure in those who are delicate and have bodies with hidden veins.
And when you want to cure it and the patient feels that pain, then do not appear to the heart as we have said, but press tightly over that and move below it slightly and dry over it so that the winding contraction is evacuated, and cauterize the site.
But if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure that by excising the body and by evacuating the windings, and cauterize those with smelly pustules and pustules of serapi and similar ones.
Of extracting arrows.
Arrows are diversified according to the species, and according to the parts of the body where they are stuck, because their diversity is that some have great points, and small ones, and concave ones, and smooth ones, and solid ones; and some have three angles, and others have tongues, and still others are astral.
And the signs of the brain are when it sticks into it an arrow and pierces the bone, and there occurs in the head a violent headache, and scotomia, and vertigo, and heat in the eyes, and inflammation and heat in the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile, and the words are cut off and the voice is destroyed, and pus comes out from the site of the wound moist like milk, and there appear from it marks like drops of blood.
And so if these signs appear to you, then abstain from the cure and extracting of the arrow unless it is out.
But the signs of the arrow when it sticks into the heart are that it is near the left milk vein, and it feels as if it were stuck in a hard cause, and it is not a soft cause; and then the movement of the arrow is like the movement of the pulse, and it runs from the wound black blood, and there appears freezing of the extremities, and fainting, and syncopes; and then you will know that death is coming upon him.
When the arrow has pierced the lung, foam-like blood flows from the wound and the vessels near the neck are swollen; the patient's color changes, he exhales with great effort, and asks for air to breathe.
And if the arrow pierces the membrane in the foot, and the pain is near the small ribs, a great wound with intense pain and sighing occur, and not all the members of the muscles are affected.
And if the arrow pierces the stomach, then a little blood flows from the wound with some indigestible food.
And if the arrow pierces the belly and is stuck in it, blood flows from a wound in the membrane or intestine which has been ruptured, and there is no hope for a cure unless the arrow is removed.
And if the arrow pierces the bladder and urine flows out, and some cause proceeds from it to the genitals, and great pain occurs in the patient, then know that it is fatal.
But the other members such as the face, neck, jaw, shoulders, spine, breastbone, groin, thigh and their like in the members are saved according to the greatest dispositions when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery, and it is not a venomous arrow.
And I will recount to you what I have seen of the nature of these arrows, so that you may understand through this about your treatment.
The cause is that once an arrow pierced the tear duct in the corner of his eye near the nose, and I extracted it from him through the other opening without hurting the eye, and he was healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a Jew who had it in the corner of his eye below the eyelid; the arrow was already concealed and he had only a small end protruding to which some fur stuck, and it was a large arrow of the acute arrows of the Turks with an iron tip shaped like a lion's claw, and there were no eyelids.
And the Jew was saved, and his eye did not suffer any ill effect.
And I extracted another arrow from a Christian man which had pierced his jaw and was an Arabic arrow to which eyelids were attached; then I inserted it between two fingers and it was already submerged in his jaw, and I pulled it out gently and the Christian was healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a man which had pierced his belly, and I thought he would die from it; but then since thirty days passed without any change in his condition according to his dispositions, I inserted my finger into the wound and probed around, and he was healed, and no ill effect occurred to him.
And I saw a man in whom an arrow had pierced his back and the wound was closed over him; but then after fire burned him for seven years, the arrow emerged from the root of his thigh.
And I saw a woman in whom an arrow had pierced her belly and the wound was closed inside her, and she did not change in any of her natural operations for three years, and the woman did not suffer any harm in any of her natural operations.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow had pierced his face and the wound was closed, and the arrow broke but he did not feel pain, and similar things happened to him.
And I extracted an arrow from the prince of the king's son who had it in the bridge of his nose and it had turned slightly to the right; the entire arrow was concealed.
And I was called to heal him when the arrow was extracted after three days.
Then I probed the wound of the arrow gently and he did not feel it, but he felt a pricking under his right eyelid, and then I perceived that this pricking was from the tip of the arrow.
And I applied ointment to the wound with an astringent and digestive mixture, believing that the location would become apparent to me where the arrow was, so it would heal over it.
And no significant incident occurred to the location where the arrow had pierced; and I continued applying the ointment for several days, and no incident occurred; but then the wound closed up, and the piercing was healed over the course of several days until one day he felt the arrow within his nose and notified me.
Then I applied sharp corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until pus opened up; and through probing gently, I discovered the tip of the arrow which was sticking to the bone.
Then I applied that sharp medicine to the wound until it appeared to me visibly, and I waited with it for a period of four months.
Then when the wound was enlarged and I could insert the forceps into it without resistance, and it did not yield to pulling, then I ceased probing gently and began using methods of traction with instruments made for this purpose until one day while working on the wound with these instruments, I extracted the arrow; and then I restored that wound.
And some doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose was not restored, but I restored it and the wound healed over, and the patient was entirely healthy and did not suffer in any way.
And I recommend to you the quality of extracting some arrows so that you understand the rule and significance of what I have not said, for the parts of this article and its definitions are not comprehended by narration nor understood by the mind.
And the wise craftsman compares a little with much; and from that which is present to that which is absent, and finds a new operation and an unknown instrument, he infers the descent of strange causes when it happens.
Therefore I say that arrows are not extracted from the parts in which they are stuck, but according to two methods: either by attraction of the location where they pierce, or by repulsion from the other side.
And that which is stuck by the location it enters is an arrow proceeding from a fleshy location and is pulled and extracted.
And if it does not yield to being pulled at the hour in which it pierces, then cover it for several days until the flesh around it becomes swollen and the entrance of it is pushed out and its exit.
And similarly if it is stuck in bones and does not yield to you, then leave it for several days and repeat pulling and motion on each day, and it is extracted.
And if it does not yield to you after several days, then cover that you pierce around the arrow in that bone on all sides with a subtle bore until the location is enlarged by the arrow, and then extract it.
But if the arrow is deeply lodged in the body and feels sensitive, then you should probe it with a thin instrument suitable for extraction.
And if you cannot access it due to the tightness of the flesh and the length of the arrowhead, and there are no bones or nerves or veins in the way, then you should cut through the flesh around the arrowhead so that it is loose enough for extraction.
And if there are nails holding it in place, then you should loosen the flesh around them with any instrument you can find; and if you cannot access the nail itself due to the swelling of the flesh or the torque on the nail, then cut through the swollen flesh around the nail so that it can be removed.
And when you are extracting the arrow from any part of the body, use your hand and forceps with all your strength to pull it out; and if it is difficult to remove due to its position, then cut through the flesh around it with a sharp instrument so that it can be removed easily without breaking.
And if you cannot reach it at that moment, then leave it for a few days until the swelling around it goes down, and then try again when it is less difficult to reach. But if you are facing a flow of blood, then treat it as we have described in the relevant chapter.
And be careful not to cut any veins or nerves, or damage any internal organs; use all the methods we have described to you with caution, and do so slowly, calmly, and firmly, as we have instructed.
And when you are pulling out the arrow, make sure that the patient is in a position that allows for easy removal of the arrow, as this will be more beneficial for them. But if this is not possible for you, then do what you can according to the figures provided.
But arrows that are shot in the opposite direction, or those that have already exited one side and entered another, or those that cause pain when they are pulled from the upper part of the body, then you should cut off their tip; and you will know where to cut according to how much space there is between the jaws of your forceps; and then pull it out, as this will make extraction easier.
But if it is lodged in the bone, then you should twist a wire in the opposite direction to how the arrow is embedded in the bone, and increase the pressure until it becomes loose, and then pull it out.
And if not, then leave it for a few days, and then try again when it has become looser.
And if the shaft of the arrow is inside him, then you should push it out.
But if the shaft is broken and you want to administer an injection, then insert it into the hollow shaft of the arrow and push it through so that it exits through the tip.
But if the arrow is hollow, then push it out with a strong instrument inserted into it, as the arrow will be pushed out by this action.
And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut away all the flesh around it that has been infected by the poison, as far as you can; and then treat it with what is appropriate.
And if the arrow pierces the foot, or stomach, or bladder, or side, and you can touch it with your fingers, then cut through the flesh around it so that you can reach it; be careful not to cut any veins or nerves, and then pull it out, and close the wound if necessary, and treat it until it is healed.
The shape of the forceps used for pulling out arrows:
If you are unable to remove the arrow due to some contrary cause, then leave it for a few days or weeks, and then try again when it has become looser. The ends of the forceps should be shaped like an owl's beak, with teeth that grip the arrow so that it does not slip out.
And they should be made in different sizes, large and small, depending on the size of the arrow, the thickness of the flesh, the width of the wound, and the tightness of the area.
It should be shaped like a ray so that it pushes against the arrow inside the hollow shaft and is pushed out by this action.

But if you are in the days of summer, then you are excused from immersing his hand in warm water; and the blood is put into warm water in wintertime.
And the phlebotomy of this vein is safer than all other veins, for beneath it there is no pulsating vein nor nerve.

And beware of not completing the phlebotomy with your hand, for beneath are the nerves of the teeth, bared of flesh.
And you should immerse his hand in the warm water and let the blood run into that, for if you do not immerse his hand in the warm water, the blood will coagulate at the opening of the vein, and flow is prohibited.

Thus begins the treatment of the third part: of restoration. This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine; and it is restoration of fracture and of dislocation accidental in the bones.
